Current Affairs Commentary

Huang and Su Loan Negotiations Fail 18

— Yu

A Reuters dispatch from London recently reported that commercial loan negotiations were underway between Britain and the Soviet Union. Britain intended to provide a loan to the Soviet Union for the purpose of purchasing British goods such as railway materials, and it was said that a portion of the loan amount might be used to repay part of the old debts owed to Britain from the Tsarist era. However, according to TASS news, these negotiations did not take place. The Soviet authorities also stated that pre-revolutionary loans were completely unrelated to current loan issues and that the Soviet Union would not allow them to be mentioned in the same breath.

In recent years, Anglo-Soviet relations have fluctuated between tension and relaxation. The opposition of political systems is the root cause of the inability of the two countries to truly be on good terms. Soviet assistance to colonies seeking to secede from their mother countries, British arrangements for an anti-Soviet front, and the issue of repaying old debts have all caused the relationship between the two parties to often trend toward isolation. However, we cannot assume that there will be absolutely no room for coordination between the two countries. There are indeed many areas where they mutually benefit. To name the most obvious, Britain is eagerly anticipating the Soviet Union's vast market, and the Soviet Union is also very willing to accept the assistance of foreign capital. Moreover, in terms of the current international situation, the recent tensions in the Far East and Europe and Africa may somewhat ease the degree of opposition between the two countries. Although the rumors of loan negotiations from London this time have not been realized, it can be imagined that the British side already has this intention. According to our observation, it seems that this time Britain's needs from the Soviet Union are more urgent than the Soviet Union's needs from Britain. Let us elaborate.

First, in recent years, Britain's foreign markets have been shrinking. The penetration of goods and capital from Japan, the United States, and other countries into the colonies has been quite profound. Currently, the Japanese influence in the Chinese market is shaking Britain's inherent superior position. Canada's tendency to lean toward the United States is becoming increasingly apparent. Many Britons believe that the newly revised US-Canada trade agreement means that Canada's affiliation with Britain will inevitably lose its meaning one day. They are also worried about the collapse of the Ottawa Imperial Trade Agreement. All of this is enough to prove the distress of British goods and capital seeking outlets. The Soviet Union has a vast territory and rich purchasing power, making it an excellent market.

Second, the League of Nations' sanctions against Italy have made the situation in Europe and Africa quite precarious. (Recently, there was also the outbreak of the Egyptian demand for complete independence.) Japan has penetrated deeply into China, and the situation in the Pacific is treacherous. Based on these extremely tense international situations, Britain needs a strong supporter in the Far East and the Near East. The Soviet Union, dominating Eurasia, is a good target for Britain.

As for the Soviet Union, in order to implement its policy of peace to facilitate the completion of domestic construction, it is happy to maintain better relations with Britain. It also has a great need to utilize foreign capital for construction, so borrowing from Britain to purchase goods should also be expected by the Soviet Union.

However, hope is one thing, and whether the facts can be achieved is another. Currently, Anglo-Soviet relations do have the above-mentioned conditions for mutual benefit. But it is not entirely true to say that the loan will certainly be established and that relations will certainly be close. The future of these negotiations will likely face at least the following difficulties, which must be overcome.

1. The issue of political opposition: If Britain does not stop its role as an anti-Red protagonist, or if the Soviet Union does not give up its assistance to colonial revolutions, the relationship between the two countries will have no way to improve.

2. The issue of old debts: If the Soviet Union expresses its unwillingness to repay the old debts of the Tsarist era, then the British public will definitely oppose taking on new debts, which may cause a considerable setback in the negotiations.

3. Trade issues: It is said that both Britain and the Soviet Union have expressed their hope to expand export trade. Then, during negotiations on trade agreements, a state of opposition may arise.

In conclusion, we believe that Anglo-Soviet negotiations are by no means a simple matter. Even if the two countries can reach some kind of agreement in the future, it is feared that it will not be possible to proceed without following a winding path.

Anglo-French Negotiations Highly Satisfactory; Opportunity for Peace Talks Matures Again; Sanctions Against Italy Proceeding Satisfactorily; Laval Expresses Firm Stance Towards Italy 19

(London) According to official announcements, the talks between French Prime Minister Laval and British Ambassador Clerk yesterday were "highly satisfactory" and can almost be considered a shortcut to restoring peace in Abyssinia. As for British Foreign Office Abyssinia expert Penderson, he is still in Paris talking with French Foreign Office Director of East Africa, Sangandan. The Foreign Office has already received Penderson's report, but it believes that before the talks can continue to progress, the Foreign Office must first conduct a thorough study of the report. (Havas dispatch on the 28th)

(Paris) The Associated Press learned today from absolutely reliable sources that France has sternly replied to Italy's warning regarding the implementation of the oil embargo. Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval met with Italian Ambassador Cerutti today and delivered the reply in person. It is understood that Laval also warned Italy that any acts of war, such as an Italian attack on British warships, would be considered an act of war against all member states of the League of Nations, and France would not be able to stand aside. The leaders of Britain and France believe that the time for peace negotiations is now ripe, and it is understood that the British and French ambassadors to Italy have both been ordered to meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini to secretly express the conditions for stopping the war in East Africa. Laval believes that Italy will accept the non-Amhara provinces that the Italian army has already conquered as conditions for a truce, so he is eager to conduct diplomatic negotiations to prevent Mussolini from taking risks after the world implements the oil embargo. As for Mussolini's claim that Italy will consider the oil embargo as an act of war and will respond with an act of war, opinions here are divided as to whether this is a bluff or whether Italy is indeed prepared to launch a European war. (National Press dispatch on the 28th)

(Paris) British Ambassador to France Clerk paid a visit to Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval the day before yesterday and held talks. According to the Paris Echo and Business Daily, the British ambassador told Laval that Italy had misunderstood France's attitude and that a dangerous international situation had arisen. Therefore, Laval should notify Rome that the British and French views are completely consistent. The British ambassador also said that Italy mistakenly believes that France is taking a neutral stance on the Italo-Abyssinian issue. It must be known that if an Italian warship were to bomb any British warship in the Mediterranean, it would not only be an act of aggression against the British Empire but also an act of aggression against all member states of the League of Nations, including France. Therefore, the French Prime Minister should immediately notify the Italian government that if Italy carries out its threats, cooperation between Britain and France will be inevitable. Laval, upon hearing the British ambassador's words, agreed to do so. When Laval received Italian Ambassador Cerutti yesterday, he seemed to have told him that if Italy were to take risks, the consequences would be unimaginable. (Havas dispatch on the 29th)

(Paris) The London Daily Mail points out that Laval's conversation with the Italian ambassador has dispelled the doubts of last week and says that the sanctions implemented in Geneva next week will make Italy's war unsustainable. (Reuters dispatch on the 29th)

(Geneva) Italy's threatening remarks in response to the proposal to impose an oil embargo may not sway the views of various countries. Current general opinion strongly advocates that the Committee of Eighteen should meet early next week to show that the League of Nations is determined to deal with this issue. However, French Prime Minister Laval will be unable to come to Geneva next week, so the Committee of Eighteen may not be able to meet until the second week of December. Although some quarters believe that Laval's attitude is to delay the decision, it is widely believed that if the Committee of Eighteen decides on an oil embargo, France will not obstruct its implementation. The League of Nations is confident that if Geneva takes action, the United States will actively follow suit. (Reuters dispatch on the 29th)

(Geneva) According to a British government representative from the sanctions expert committee studying the sanctions issue, the plan to ban the transport of raw materials to Italy is proceeding quite satisfactorily. (Reuters dispatch on the 29th)

Chairman of the Committee of Eighteen Contacts Regarding Meeting Date; French Foreign Minister Answers That He Is Willing to Attend in Person 20

(Geneva) The chairman of the Committee of Eighteen, Portuguese representative Vasco Gonçalves, contacted representatives of the governments of the countries concerned by telephone for the purpose of setting a meeting date. French Prime Minister Laval replied that he was still willing to attend in person. Vasco Gonçalves intends to decide on a date this afternoon. (Havas dispatch on the 29th)

(London) The Committee of Eighteen was originally scheduled to meet tomorrow, but the meeting was postponed because French Prime Minister Laval was detained in Paris due to domestic political affairs and did not have time to go to Geneva. According to news from Geneva, the host country representative of the League of Nations, Portuguese representative Vasco Gonçalves, may decide on a new date for the meeting tomorrow. The duties of the committee are to accept the reports of the experts handling economic and financial sanctions against Italy and to continue to consider the proposal submitted by the Canadian representative and approved in principle by various countries to ban the transport of coal, iron, and oil to Italy. (Reuters dispatch on the 28th)

Italian Troops Busy with Movements; Increased Defenses in Both North and South 21

(London) Roman officials remain tight-lipped about the recent troop movements, but according to travelers arriving in South Tyrol, large-scale troop movements are currently underway in northern Italy. Of the seven divisions under the control of the Bolzano Command, only three divisions remain to defend the Brenner Pass, the lowest mountain pass in the Alps and the gateway to Italy from Germany. It is said that in the past 48 hours, three Italian divisions have been transferred from Riara to the border between Italy and France. A regiment of light cavalry will also travel to southern Italy to take on special duties related to coastal defense. It is also said that a large number of military supplies are currently being transported from South Tyrol to southern Italy. Northern Italy stationed 500,000 troops this summer, but after the current transfer is completed, the troops stationed in northern Italy will be less than 30,000, which shows the importance of the Brenner Pass. The situation in Italy at the moment does not seem as tense as elsewhere. Residents of South Tyrol are alarmed by rumors that Mussolini will soon issue a general mobilization order and that soldiers and Blackshirt comrades will not be allowed to take leave. (Reuters dispatch on the 29th)

(Rome) A special dispatch from our reporter: The movement of Italian main force troops in recent days is a precautionary measure to cope with all future events, not only to strengthen the defenses of the Alps. The Italian government has not increased troops in the African colony of Libya, nor does it intend to reduce the garrison there, because the issue of the balance of power in the Mediterranean will be raised at the London Naval Conference, and there is no need to take urgent action at this time. Officials are keeping the troop movements secret, and no newspapers have published a word about them, but it is generally known that this action also serves to support diplomatic activities, so as to prevent countries participating in sanctions from banning the import of oil into Italy. (Havas dispatch on the 29th)

Italian Cabinet Meeting Today 22

(Rome) It was announced here today that the Italian Cabinet will hold a meeting at 10 a.m. on Saturday. (National Press dispatch on the 28th)

New Italian Military Commander Takes Office 23

Asmara. Italian Army Chief of Staff General Badoglio arrived here today and immediately took office as High Commissioner of Italian East Africa and Commander-in-Chief of the Italian Army invading Abyssinia. He immediately began to study the military reports from the various fronts. The previous Commander-in-Chief, General De Bono, met with General Badoglio at Massawa before departing for Italy. (National Press dispatch on the 28th)

Italy Resists Sanctions; Music from Various Countries Also Boycotted; Only Shakespeare and Shaw Exempted; Gold Collection Proceeding Actively 24

(Rome) Italy's resistance to sanctions has even affected music and drama. The Propaganda Ministry has ordered a ban on the performance of plays and musical scores by writers from countries participating in the sanctions, with the exception of the works of British playwrights Shakespeare and Shaw and French writers, because the French intellectual class has a more moderate attitude toward Italy. In various concerts, the music of countries participating in the sanctions is also being censored. Performers, singers, and dancers from countries participating in the sanctions are not allowed to perform in Italy. Radio stations are not allowed to broadcast music from countries participating in the sanctions, with the exception of France. (Havas dispatch on the 28th)

(Rome) The gold collection campaign is still proceeding actively. Prime Minister Mussolini's wife and his eldest daughter, the Countess Ciano, recently donated one kilogram of gold and fifty kilograms of silver to the Fascist Club. (Havas dispatch on the 29th)

Italian Air Force in the South Drops 1,500 Bombs; Abyssinian Casualties Relatively Few 25

Addis Ababa. The Italian Air Force is still active on the southern front, dropping 1,500 bombs on Daggah Bur today. According to an Abyssinian communiqué, Abyssinian casualties were relatively few. At the same time, officials in Rome deny reports that the Abyssinian army has recaptured Walwal. (Reuters dispatch on the 29th)

Italian Army Front in the North. The Italian military is optimistic about the various rumors surrounding the diplomatic negotiations being conducted by Britain and France in Paris, saying that an agreement should be reached soon. However, it still believes that after the new Commander-in-Chief, General Badoglio, takes office, he will definitely follow the original plan to launch a major battle with the enemy army to determine victory or defeat, as if there were no peace talks in Paris. General Badoglio has recently appointed his son as director of the Chief of Staff's confidential office, and he does not intend to make any changes to the staff. (Havas dispatch on the 29th)

Abyssinian Emperor Inspects Troops on the Northern Front 26

Addis Ababa. The Abyssinian Emperor traveled by car to Tesci, in the Wolo province of the northern front, at 10:15 a.m. yesterday to inspect the troops and encourage morale. The entourage consisted of three cars and four trucks. The Minister of Finance, the Minister of Posts and Telecommunications, the Emperor's private secretary, and the royal physician were in the same car as the Emperor. The Empress, along with the two princesses and the youngest son, traveled in another car, but only accompanied the Emperor for 20 kilometers before returning to the capital. Other dignitaries, such as former Army Minister Balu, traveled in the third car. Two trucks were used to transport food, and two trucks were used to carry 25 guards. The Emperor traveled incognito, but the heavy security in front of the palace at the time of departure allowed the people to surmise that the Emperor was on tour. Many residents surrounded the palace, cheering and paying respects to the imperial vehicle. Last night, the Emperor stayed overnight in Teblatpong, 150 kilometers from the capital. He is expected to arrive in Tesci tonight and then fly to the front line in Tigray province for inspection. Mules and trucks transported food along the Emperor's route. (Havas dispatch on the 29th)

French Cabinet Wins Confidence of Parliament; Rome Relieved; Sees as a Favorable Factor in International Developments; Franc Avoids Devaluation, Pleasing Impact on Italian Currency 27

(Rome) Political circles here are extremely pleased to hear that the French Chamber of Deputies has passed a vote of confidence in the Laval cabinet. The continued existence of the Laval cabinet is seen here as a favorable factor in the progress of the international situation. Since France joined the sanctions policy, Italian officials have been quite uneasy, but this uneasiness has now been completely eliminated. Political circles now hope that peace negotiations can be successful before the scope of the embargo is expanded. (Havas dispatch on the 28th)

(Rome) Officials here were pleased to hear that French Prime Minister Laval achieved a preliminary victory in the Chamber of Deputies today, which avoided the devaluation of the franc. An important Italian official stated today that the French government's winning the vote of confidence can be seen as a continuation of French policy, and avoiding the panic of the franc's devaluation will have a pleasing impact on the Italian currency. (Reuters dispatch on the 28th)

Anglo-Russian Negotiations Fail to Resolve Old Debt Issues; Far Eastern Situation Promotes Rapprochement Between the Two Countries — Observations from a Parisian Left-Wing Newspaper 28

(Moscow) Some foreign newspapers have claimed that an Anglo-Soviet loan agreement would be concluded because former British holders of old Russian bonds would receive partial compensation. TASS learned from the Soviet authorities that the two sides had never held negotiations on this agreement and could not negotiate on it because pre-revolutionary debts were completely unrelated to the current loan issue and the Soviet Union would never allow them to be mentioned in the same breath. (TASS dispatch on the 28th)

Paris, World Press dispatch. The influential left-wing organization "L'Œuvre" predicted in an editorial that after the new developments in North China, there would be an early union between Britain and Russia. Observers in British diplomatic circles believed that the only way left for Britain to resist Japan's actions in China was to reach an understanding with Soviet Russia regarding the two countries' actions in the Far East. The newspaper believed that to promote this understanding, the British government would lend the Soviet Union a loan of £25 million to £45 million in exchange for the Soviet capital's gold reserves being deposited in the Bank of England in order to stabilize the exchange rate of the ruble.

Greek King Begins Reign by Granting Amnesty to Political Prisoners; Willing to Resign to Argue the Case; Demetrios Ordered to Form Cabinet 29

Chinese Antiquities on Public Display in London 30

(London) Chinese antiquities were publicly exhibited today at Burlington House in London. The exhibit includes 4,000 items, of which approximately 800 were specially obtained from the Forbidden City in Beijing by the Chinese government. The British monarch also contributed several Chinese antiquities to the display. The largest item in the venue is a Buddha statue, said to weigh 20 tons. The smallest items include bronze mirrors dating back over 2,000 years. The jade artifacts are particularly exquisite, including a jade钺 (battle-axe) from 2000 BC. There are also three jade seals connected to each other by delicate chains, carved from a single piece of rare yellow jade. In addition to porcelain, pottery, bronze, and textiles, there are also masterpieces of calligraphy, painting, and lacquer carving. According to experts, the collection of so many Chinese art objects in one place is a grand occasion unprecedented in history. (28th, Reuters)

Chinese Ambassador Guiding the British Monarch and Queen to Visit Chinese Antiquities Tomorrow 31

(London) The Chinese art exhibition is extremely popular. The British monarch and queen will visit the exhibition, and will be guided by Chinese Ambassador Guo Taiqi. (29th, Reuters)

Brazilian Uprising Suppressed; Government Forces Able to Control the Overall Situation 32

Rio de Janeiro: The Brazilian government announced today that the revolutionary party has been completely suppressed in all undisturbed areas, and federal troops have control of the entire situation. Documents obtained by the police prove that the disturbances of the past few days were instigated by Communist leader Prestes. The government is now conducting a massive search for Prestes, the severity of which sets a new record for Brazil. It is noted that Prestes was recently elected as a member of the Executive Committee of the Third International. (28th, Central News Agency)

Stalin's Mother 33

Tbilisi Correspondent: A correspondent from TASS visited Stalin's mother, Ekaterina, and wrote the following:

We entered a small, cozy apartment with many well-lit, simply furnished rooms. The first thing that caught our eye was a huge photograph of Lenin. On a round table was a vase filled with fresh flowers, and several recent newspapers. On a sofa in front of the table sat Stalin's mother, simply dressed with a black shawl over her head. She wore horn-rimmed glasses and was reading a newspaper when we entered. We shook her old, thin hand. When we spoke about her son, her eyes filled with joy, expressing her tenderness and contentment. She said:

"I met with Soso... It had been a long time since I had seen him. My health is not good, and I often feel weak, but when I saw him, I was extremely happy, as if I had grown a pair of wings. My weakness and illness vanished.

"Our Lavrentiy (Secretary of the Regional Committee of the Federal Communist Party) said that Soso had arrived, that he was here, and could come in at any time.

"The door opened, and he stepped over the threshold. It was my own son! I looked and could hardly believe my old eyes. He was very happy too; he ran over and kissed me. He looked very well, happy, joyful, and tenderly asked about my health, relatives, and friends.

"Suddenly, I saw the silver strands in my son's hair. I said, 'What's this? Son! Has your hair turned gray too?' He replied, 'Don't worry about it, Mother! Gray hair doesn't matter. I feel very good. Don't worry about my hair.'

"I also asked about my grandchildren. I love them more than anything in the world! My Svetlana, Yasha, and Vanso. Soso joked that Svetlana had sent him to ask Grandma for some plum jam. Soso also loves plum jam; he has been like that since he was little.

"Time passed quickly. We are all old now, friends and relatives. He told many jokes, and we laughed. We sat together for a long time; I was very happy because I had Soso with me.

"Later, Soso went to see his friends, and I stayed home alone. I thought about the past. Besides Soso, I had two other sons, but they died early, leaving only him. I thought about how I wanted to educate my son, how I sent him to school in Gori (a small town in the Caucasus). He was a good student. But his father, my late husband Vissarion, decided to take him out of school to teach him his own trade! To be a shoemaker.

"I did my best to oppose it, even arguing with my husband, but it was no use; he had his way.

"But after a short time, I was victorious again and sent Soso back to school. He was considered one of the best students in the school and received a stipend of three rubles per day."

We listened quietly and attentively to the old lady's slow speech. She told us about her life with her son in Gori: to make a living, she had to do all kinds of hard work herself. She spoke of how her son read as a child, and how he taught others; even as a small child, he taught many neighboring children to read and write.

She also talked about other times, about when Stalin began to do revolutionary work. She spoke of the bitter days she lived through when her son was in exile in Siberia.

We looked with her at a photograph of Stalin as a child, a family photo from when he entered high school. We looked at her corner wall, where several of Stalin's best photographs were hung, right by her bed. On one of the photos was Stalin's autograph written in Georgian.

Mrs. Ekaterina continued: "Soso soon returned from his walk with his friends. We talked for a long time again. I treated him with all the best things, and didn't forget to give him a jar of plum jam to take to Svetlana.

"But the time was short; the time for parting came too quickly. Soso ran over and kissed me very gently. I was reluctant to part with him, and tears came to my eyes, but I restrained myself. I didn't want my son to know how reluctant I was to let him go, because I knew very well that he was busy and had many important things to do."

That is how our visit ended. We bid her farewell, thanking her for her warm hospitality, and left her deeply moved! The room of the old woman who had given the world its great leader. (TASS)

Stalin's Mother

Page 7

French Parliament Debates Budget; Agenda Prioritizes Finance Over Party Disputes; Laval Cabinet Achieves Preliminary Victory Yesterday 34

(Paris) The Chamber of Deputies resumed its meeting at 9:30 this morning to discuss the government's financial policy. A small number of deputies were in attendance, including Premier and Foreign Minister Laval and Finance Minister Regnier. Communist Deputy Dorès and Socialist Deputy Olivier spoke in succession, attacking the government's current policy, stating that the government's delegated legal decrees had failed to balance the budget. Although wages had been greatly reduced, economic recovery had not been effective, and retail prices had not decreased. Left-wing Republican Deputy Daladier then spoke in support of the government, saying that if a cabinet change were to occur, all hope for economic recovery would vanish, which would be extremely dangerous. At this point, Radical Party Deputy Clerc rose to refute the arguments made by the Communist Deputy, saying that the standard of living had decreased by 28% in the last four years. The Chamber of Deputies then extended the meeting until 3:00 PM to continue the discussion. (29th, Havas)

(Paris) Today was the day the French Parliament reconvened. A light rain fell on the streets of Paris, and pedestrians could not linger, so the whole city was quiet and no disturbances were seen. The Chamber of Deputies met at 3:10 PM. Premier Laval immediately requested the Chamber to discuss the interpellation on the government's financial policy, while the interpellation on the activities of fascist groups would be discussed next Tuesday. The Chamber then began to debate the procedural issue, causing controversy. Premier Laval said, "In terms of domestic affairs, the financial problem is the most urgent at present. The government must have full authority to deal with the financial crisis, so it cannot be delayed until after this afternoon." Blum, the leader of the orthodox socialists, spoke out against the discussion procedure proposed by Laval, saying, "If the government wants to unite with the parliament and gain the parliament's trust, why did it delay until November 28th to convene the parliament? The delay in the resumption of sessions of both chambers this time has already broken the previous record. It seems Laval could delay the date of convening the parliament again, and then the budget for next year could be promulgated by delegated legal decrees." Blum's words were sarcastic. Laval replied calmly, "Yes, if that were possible, I would do it." At this time, the extreme left deputies responded with jeers. (According to comments from deputies after the adjournment, Laval's words meant that the government could temporarily use the 1935 budget as the budget for next year, as the previous Poincaré cabinet had done.) Blum then advised the Chamber, saying that the deputies of the Chamber were mostly Republicans, and should now rise up to criticize the government. At this point, Premier Laval treated the procedural issue as a question of confidence in the government, and immediately put it to a vote. In the end, the vote of confidence in the government passed by a majority of 345 votes to 225, adopting the discussion procedure proposed by Premier Laval. Speaker Puisson then announced the start of the discussion on the interpellation on financial policy. Only one or two deputies spoke, and the Chamber adjourned at 6:50 PM, to continue the discussion tomorrow morning. The interpellation on financial policy will likely be discussed tomorrow morning and afternoon, and then a vote will be taken. The interpellation on the activities of fascist groups will be discussed next Tuesday, so the fate of the Laval cabinet will be decided after the debate next Tuesday. On the question of the vote of confidence in the government today, the number of votes cast by the Radical Socialist Party was crucial. Of the 160 seats held by Radical Socialist deputies, about 80 voted in favor of the vote of confidence, more than 50 voted against the vote of confidence, and more than 20 abstained. All of the 95 Socialist deputies, 10 Communist deputies, and 15 other extreme left deputies voted against the vote of confidence in the government. (28th, Havas)

(Paris) This afternoon, the Chamber of Deputies passed a vote of confidence in the government by a vote of 345 to 225. This indicated that the Chamber of Deputies agreed with Premier Laval's request to debate the government's financial policy first. The authorities initially feared that the government would be overthrown or riots would occur during the Chamber's debate today, so they took strict precautions and maintained local order during the debate. Another 170 guards were stationed near the Chamber of Deputies with live ammunition to prevent accidents. Today's meeting started at 3:00 PM and adjourned at 7:00 PM. The meeting will continue tomorrow morning at 9:30. The financial debate will likely end tomorrow night, and the Premier can be assured of majority support. Today's meeting was related to the survival of the government, and all cabinet members were in attendance. After the deputies were seated, Laval rose and declared that he would not evade the debate, and also said that the leaders of the various parties had held a meeting and decided to include the discussion on the affairs of the Fascist Party and the National League on the agenda for Tuesday morning, and also decided to discuss the budget bill this afternoon. Everyone applauded to express their approval. Laval continued, saying that if the Chamber was willing, the government intended to allow discussion of Mr. Deng Wen's report on the Fascist Party and the National Federation, and the government did not intend to avoid any responsibility, but if a vote of confidence was to be held, then all votes should be cast. Leader of the inflationists, Reynaud, then declared that all political disturbances must be stopped now, and the budget bill should be discussed first. Socialist leader Blum opposed delaying the discussion of the affairs of the Fascist Party and the National Federation, so a vote of confidence in the government was held. Of the 160 Radical Party deputies, 8 voted for the government, 50 voted against, and the rest either abstained or were absent. All of the extreme left parties voted against the government. (28th, Reuters)

Completing the Entire Journey in Five Days; "China Clipper" Arrives in Manila; Crossing the Pacific Ocean, a Journey of 8,000 Miles; Opening a New Era of Transportation Between America and the Far East 35

(Manila) The "China Clipper," the first large flying boat to carry mail across the Pacific Ocean, has now completed its entire journey and landed in Manila Bay at 3:36 this afternoon. Several hundred people watched. The plane departed from San Francisco six days ago, but actually flew for only five days. It stopped in Guam for one day for Thanksgiving. After the plane landed, 100,000 letters were taken out, mostly sent by stamp collectors in the United States. The letters and parcels will be transported to the post office by special vehicles, and then the post office will sort out those destined for China and send them to Hong Kong by mail ship. Captain Edsick and the other pilots then went ashore and said that they had departed from Guam this morning and no accidents had occurred en route. It has not yet been announced when the plane will fly back to the United States, but it will probably be in a few days. (29th, Central News Agency)

(Manila) The 25-ton China Clipper flying boat, which took off from Alameda on October 22nd to make the first regular mail flight across the Pacific, should arrive here this afternoon. The time will be around 3:30 or 4:00. Manila is preparing to welcome it with great excitement. It is expected that the entire city's population will come out to see the large flying boat land. It is believed that a new era in the relationship between the United States and the Philippines will begin from this point. This boat will complete the unprecedented 8,000-mile journey today. It is carrying two tons of mail. When it first flew from San Francisco to Honolulu, there were only seven people on board, but when it took off from Honolulu, it carried a total of fourteen people. (29th, Reuters)

Manila: The China Clipper landed here at 3:30 this afternoon, taking seven days to complete its 8,500-mile journey from San Francisco to Manila. When the flying boat landed in Manila Bay, the spectators along the coast cheered. Several naval aircraft soared through the sky, and warships in the harbor fired salutes to pay their respects. After Captain Musick landed, the representative of Manila presented him with the keys to the city. Musick then gave a radio address, expressing his gratitude for the warm welcome in the Philippines, and said that it was only after more than five years of long and careful preparation that it was possible to make the journey. Musick later presented President Quezon with a special letter from President Roosevelt. This boat came from Guam, traveling 1,700 miles and rising to an altitude of 10,000 feet, without seeing any ships. It is now scheduled to fly back on December 2nd. The Philippine Post Office has sold stamps worth US$25,000. This boat is the largest aircraft built by the United States, can carry 51,000 pounds, and has a maximum speed of 180 miles per hour, powered by four 800-horsepower engines. Captain Musick is 41 years old, has been in the aviation industry for 22 years, has flown over 10,000 hours, and has traveled over 1 million miles without any accidents. He has an excellent record. (28th, Reuters)

(Manila) The China Clipper arrived over here at 3:00 this afternoon, circled for about half an hour, and then landed. The pilot landed at 4:05 PM. The Minister of Public Works and Communications and the Mayor of Manila warmly welcomed him. The Mayor presented Captain Musick with the keys to the city of Manila. President Quezon welcomed him at the Malacañang Palace. Captain Murdock presented President Quezon with the airmail from US President Roosevelt. (29th, Central News Agency)

Guam: The China Clipper flew to Manila at 6:06 this morning. Guam Naval Governor Captain Alexander and others personally saw Captain Edsick and the plane's personnel off. 15,000 of the island's 20,000 residents watched the plane take off. (29th, Central News Agency)

Prospects for the Naval Conference; Britain Not Optimistic; US Expanding Pacific Aviation; Japan to Raise New Demands 36

(London) The Naval Conference is scheduled to open on December 6th. The political circles here are now discussing the impact of this conference on the British government's plan to expand British defense. If the major powers reach any agreement on the tonnage and types of warships, or the caliber of artillery, then British procedure will naturally be affected. It is reported that the British government believes that the more restrictions agreed upon at the Naval Conference, the less funds the British Treasury will have to raise for the naval program. The preliminary talks that have taken place have not inspired much hope for a restrictive agreement. However, the British government is not optimistic about the outcome of the conference, but hopes that some achievements can be made. The conference will be chaired by British Prime Minister Baldwin. Representatives from all major naval powers will attend. The leaders of the British delegation are Foreign Secretary Hoare and Naval Secretary Monsell. (28th, Reuters)

(London) According to diplomatic sources, the situation in the Far East will have a great impact on the Naval Conference to be held in London on December 6th. Japan will insist on demands for naval equality with Britain and the United States. Britain and the United States will reject this demand because Japan disregards the Nine-Power Treaty. The Nine-Power Treaty was one of the agreements concluded at the Washington Conference in 1922, and the naval superiority of Britain and the United States at the time was the force that brought about this situation. Therefore, if this naval superiority is not maintained, the treaty guaranteeing China's territorial integrity will be equal to waste paper. It is also reported that Britain will use the League of Nations to maintain its position in China. This is the true reason why Britain invited the League of Nations to send representatives to the Naval Conference. The British government asked Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota to explain what the Japanese army intends to do in North China, which is enough to show Britain's concern for the new situation between China and Japan. (29th, Central News Agency)

(London) The Naval Conference has been postponed to December 9th because the US delegation is unable to arrive early. (29th, Reuters)

(London) According to a report in the "Hai Ri Dian Wen Bao," when the Naval Conference opens, the Japanese representatives will likely propose to expand Article 19 of the Washington Naval Treaty, which prohibits the relevant countries from expanding naval bases in the Pacific. Japan's proposal is based on the recent opening of Pacific aviation by Pan American Airways, saying that US Pacific aviation, via Honolulu, Midway Island, Wake Island, and Guam, to Manila, is actually giving the US fleet a bridge to approach the Sea of Japan, which is of great military importance. (29th, Havas)

(Rome) The "Shi Zhe Bao" recently published an article commenting on the upcoming London Naval Conference, saying that Britain's real danger lies in the Far East. If Britain can reach an agreement with the Mediterranean powers to respect each other's rights, so that Britain can act freely in the rest of the world, that would be the best policy. (28th, Havas)

(Tokyo) US Secretary of the Navy Swanson, in response to a visit from a Washington press corps, said that the fundamental policy of the United States in the London Naval Disarmament Conference is still to adhere to building warships within the limits of the existing treaty, and to be consistent with President Roosevelt's statement that the US government absolutely opposes the world's navies falling into chaotic competition again. However, if Japan disregards its environment and resolutely makes new demands for equality to expand its navy, then the United States will definitely strengthen the military defenses of the Pacific islands as a countermeasure. If Japan demands the same naval power as the United States, then the United States will be affected and will still feel that the Pacific facilities are insufficient. Since observing the establishment of the new government in the Philippines, there has been no indication that it will build its own navy. What kind of necessity does Japan have to expand? However, the United States will never allow the Philippines to be under the threat of Japan. Moreover, Japan's new demands for naval equality will probably not be supported by the representatives of the other countries. (29th, Japanese United News Agency)

Japanese Fishing Boats Intruded into Russian Territorial Waters; Soviet Union Protested to Japan 37

(Tokyo) Soviet Ambassador to Japan Yurenev visited Foreign Minister Hirota yesterday and protested, saying that recently, in the Heilongjiang, Songhua River, and Ussuri River regions, fishing boats flying the Japanese flag have repeatedly sailed. According to the Aigun Treaty of 1858, these rivers cannot be sailed by ships other than those of the Soviet Union and "Manchukuo." He hoped that the Japanese government would crack down on this type of sailing. Foreign Minister Hirota replied that he had not heard of Japanese ships sailing, so he did not know the details. The Aigun Treaty was signed between the Soviet Union and "Manchukuo," and Japan does not bear direct responsibility. After listening to the opinions of the country concerned, Manchukuo, he will reply. Ambassador Yurenev also urged the Japanese side to respond to the issue of establishing a joint Soviet-Manchukuo committee, and then left. (29th, Dentsu Telegraph)

Talks on Rural Life 47

— Edited by Yu Qing Tang

Rural Population and Rural Land in Jiangning Moling 48

— Qiao Qiming, Jiang Jie

(1) Introduction: In the summer of the 24th year of the Republic of China (1935), 57 students from the College of Agriculture and the Agricultural Vocational School of Jinling University, led by the authors, conducted a rural social survey in the villages near Moling Town, Jiangning County. Moling Town is located in the southeast of the capital, 25.61 kilometers from Nanjing. The Nanjing-Jian Automotive Road runs through it, making transportation extremely convenient. The town is quite orderly. According to the Jiangning County local autonomy system, the entire town and its neighboring dependencies are divided into 22 *li* (villages). Outside the town are the four *xiang* (townships) of Xiaoling, Renling, Xinling, and Ailing, totaling 96 villages. The two-week survey completed six types of forms: rural overview, family overview, farmer life, family property division, party affiliation, and cooperative member survey. This article comes from a portion of the materials in the rural overview, including the 11 *li* within the scope of Moling Town and 78 villages in the four *xiang*. The nine *li* in the town, which are non-agricultural, were not surveyed, and the materials for the other two *li* were incomplete and not included in the statistics. All villages in the four *xiang* were originally filled out, but due to several items in the forms asking about facts from the first year of the Republic of China, the villagers were vague and unclear, with no way to answer. To ensure the accuracy of the materials, it was better to have fewer than to risk errors, so they were not included in the statistics.

(2) The Relationship Between Population and Land: Population is a factor in the composition of society, and land is the source of living materials. Therefore, the foundation of the entire society is built on population and land. However, the compressibility of land is relatively small, while the growth and decline of population are constantly changing. If the population tends to increase, but the area of arable land remains the same, it will inevitably lead to difficulties in people's lives, followed by various serious social problems. For example, war, epidemics, crime, etc. are all results. Consequently, social culture lags behind, and the country has no way to progress.

In recent decades, the population and land problems in China have attracted great attention from all sectors. However, opinions vary, and there is no consensus. In terms of population, whether the quantity is excessive or not has become the focus of debate. In terms of land, although there is a common understanding that "farms are too small," there is a dispute over whether to focus on utilization or distribution in the improvement plan. Summarizing and generalizing it, it can be seen that the imbalance between population and land in China today has become an undeniable fact. The purpose of this article is to provide some assistance to those who study this issue, based on the survey results.

(3) Changes in Farm Households in the Past 23 Years: Why use farm households instead of population in this survey? Because the years are relatively far apart, recalling the number of households is not only easier than recalling the number of people, but also more accurate. At the same time, the population growth and decline of each household are limited, and there will definitely not be a large difference, so it is better to use farm households as the unit. During the survey, three to six elders were selected as representatives from each village to ask about the comparison of farm households in their village between the first year of the Republic of China and the 23rd year of the Republic of China. The transition between the Qing Dynasty and the Republic of China left a deeper impression on the farmers, and they had a better grasp when recalling. According to our statistics, the average number of households per village in each town and *xiang* in the 23rd year of the Republic of China ranged from 35.4 households in Renling *xiang* to 54.2 households in Xinling *xiang*, with a total average of 44.8 households per village. In Moling Town, Renling *xiang*, and part of Xiaoling *xiang*, there are more paddy fields because the Qinhuai River is available for irrigation, and land utilization has reached an extremely refined level, and the population has also reached saturation. Therefore, the average number of households per village is small. Xinling *xiang* and Ailing *xiang* are located in the northwest of Moling Town, and the terrain is undulating, with more dry land. Most of Xiaoling *xiang* also has the same situation. There is still the possibility of reclamation in the *xiang*. Although the income of farmers each year may not even be enough to pay for their own labor, it is still a way to make a living, so the number of farm households will gradually increase. However, according to Xiao Charli, a soil expert at the Beijing Geological Survey, and Xiao Boke, a geological expert, "the barren hills in the Jiangning area are not suitable for agricultural use and should only be used for forest land. Otherwise, not only will there be no profit, but excessive erosion will cause endless harm." Therefore, the future reclamation of farmland in the area is difficult to be optimistic about. Comparing the current number of households with the first year of the Republic of China, the total number of villages is 1,291 more households, with 14.5 households per village. If the total number of households in the first year of the Republic is used as the base, and the increase index of farm households in the past 23 years is calculated, it can be seen that Xiaoling, Ailing, and Xinling *xiang* have the largest increase, and Renling *xiang* has the smallest increase. If the total average of one town and four *xiang* is taken, it can be seen that the number of farm households in the past 23 years is nearly one-half more than the original number.

(4) Changes in Land in the Past 23 Years: Comparing the total area of cultivated land in the first year of the Republic with the 23rd year of the Republic, all *xiang* except Moling Town have increased. Moling Town is the core of the four *xiang*, and bears the various missions of connecting the economic and cultural aspects of the city and the countryside. In recent years, more buildings have been built near the town, and land has been encroached upon by road construction. At the same time, land utilization in the town is extremely refined, so there is no hope of reclaiming new land. If one more *mu* of land is used for non-agricultural purposes, the area of cultivated land will decrease by one *mu*. As for the increase index of each *xiang*, it is directly proportional to the aforementioned changes in farm households, with Xiaoyu *xiang* having the highest number and Renling *xiang* having the lowest number. As a result of the total average of one town and four *xiang*, the total area of cultivated land in the past 23 years has increased by one-eighth compared to the original number. (To be continued)

Nanjing-Hangzhou Garrison Air Defense Exercise Aircraft Engage in Fierce Battle Near Taihu Lake 57

(Nanjing) The 29th was the second day of the Nanjing-Hangzhou Garrison air defense exercise. In the morning, the Air Defense Headquarters dispatched aircraft in three routes to conduct reconnaissance operations in the southeast and west of the capital. They returned one after another at noon to report the completion of the mission. Other passive air defense units were concentrated to await orders. In the afternoon, the Air Defense Headquarters received a report of enemy aircraft in Hangzhou. It dispatched aircraft to Hangzhou, encountered them en route, and engaged in a fierce battle somewhere near Taihu Lake. The enemy aircraft retreated, but several other enemy aircraft approached various places in the Nanjing garrison area. The headquarters received a report from the Suzhou monitoring post at 3:18 PM that nine enemy aircraft were attacking from Suzhou at 2:17 PM, and issued an air raid alarm at 2:20 PM. More than 10,000 people from the participating units immediately mobilized and implemented traffic control. Vehicles gradually decreased, and pedestrians entered shelters. At 3:45 PM, another emergency alarm sounded, and the situation in the streets became more tense. Traffic control teams prevented pedestrians and vehicles from passing. The headquarters issued an all-clear order at 4:20 PM when the enemy aircraft retreated. The bustling city returned to its original state. However, there were many shortcomings in the traffic control in the afternoon. Pedestrians and vehicles were not effectively prevented, which was much worse than the blackout on the evening of the 28th. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

(Hangzhou) The 29th was the second day of the Nanjing-Zhenjiang-Hangzhou air defense exercise. The Hangzhou side received a report at dawn that simulated enemy army units were attacking and the air force was flying to Xiaoshan, Shaoxing, and other places, attempting to bomb Hangzhou. Our side immediately dispatched aircraft to intercept them and encountered them over Shaoxing. The two sides engaged in a fierce battle. At 8:50 AM, enemy aircraft flew over the city of Hangzhou and dropped bombs everywhere. Districts 5, 6, 7, and 8 were bombed, and fires broke out in many places, which were extinguished by the fire brigade. At the same time, various rescue teams and poison gas defense teams performed actions to rescue injured citizens and protect against poison gas. The all-clear signal was given at 10:00 AM when the enemy aircraft left, and traffic was restored throughout the city. At 10:30 AM, two bombers carrying 200-pound long-range bombs flew over West Lake and dropped them on the preset target in the center of the lake. More than 40,000 citizens went to the lakeside to watch. The aircraft circled once, and the huge bombs began to drop. Black smoke rose, and a loud noise occurred, shaking the entire city. The landing point was about ten meters away from the target. The second bomb also missed. Afterwards, eight more bombs were dropped before the target was destroyed. The people were amazed and deeply aware of the power of the bombs. The exercise ended at 11:00 AM. The afternoon exercise was suspended due to rain. A blackout exercise was still conducted from 8:00 PM to 9:30 PM in the evening. The 1st and 5th districts of Hangzhou conducted fire and rescue exercises from 8:30 PM to 9:30 PM. (Special dispatch, 29th)

Public Telegram 85

Waiting for Relief in Woyang County - To the Shanghai Shen Bao Newspaper, forwarded to all charitable organizations, government agencies, legal entities, newspapers, major Chinese and foreign philanthropists, and all fathers, brothers, uncles, sisters, and aunts across the country: Woyang is a barren and impoverished county, and it has suffered from years of disasters and bandits. The people have not had a chance to recover. Although there was a half-harvest last year, the population is large and the land is small, which is not enough to provide food for the whole year. Unexpectedly, since the beginning of summer this year, drought has raged, and there has been no rain for five months. The autumn crops have all withered, and there has been no harvest at all. The second district is the most severely affected. According to the county government's investigation, the affected area is more than 100,000 mu, and the affected population is more than 143,000, accounting for almost two-thirds of the entire district. In other districts that have been less severely affected, the autumn harvest is less than 20-30%. Many middle-class families have already run out of food. The elderly and the weak are begging from door to door, and the young and strong are seeking food everywhere. The sound of crying from hunger and cold constantly echoes in our ears. There will soon be nothing left to eat in the way of grass roots and tree bark. Even more tragic is that those who have fled have nowhere to go and have recently returned home, hanging their heads and waiting for death, a sight too terrible to behold. Now that winter has arrived and the cold wind is piercing to the bone, it is foreseen that most disaster victims will either die of hunger or freeze to death. This situation is even more tragic than the floods of the 10th and 20th years of the Republic. What wrong have the people of Woyang done to deserve such misfortune? We hope that everyone will show compassion and provide generous assistance. The more, the better, but even a small amount is greatly appreciated. Every bit of relief is like a life-saving soup. If you are willing to open your purses generously, please remit the funds to the Woyang County Government for transfer to this committee, which will distribute them separately and in a timely manner, so that the disaster victims can receive practical benefits quickly, and to live up to the benevolent intentions of those with compassionate hearts. We respectfully appeal on behalf of hundreds of thousands of disaster victims awaiting rescue, with the utmost urgency. Wang Jiwu, Chairman, Ge Lianyuan, Liu Furen, Wang Jianhua, Liu Xianggu, Zhang Shanfu, Liu Yunzhi, Wang Huixuan, Wang Zhemin, Standing Committee Members of the Woyang County Early Disaster Relief Committee in Northern Anhui, respectfully kowtow with forgiveness.

Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Library, Wang Delin, Joins the Rebels; The Provincial Government Committee Resolves to Dismiss Wang; The Entire Educational Community of the Province Issues a Declaration Denouncing the Traitor 86

Zhenjiang News: Wang Delin (style name Xiacai), Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Suzhou Library, 38 years old, a native of Wuxing, Zhejiang Province, was appointed to his post this summer. Recently, he suddenly left his post secretly to go to eastern Hebei to participate in the activities of the puppet Eastern Hebei Anti-Communist Committee, and served as a member, concurrently as the director of both the education and construction departments. It is said that before this, Wang had written to a friend in Suzhou, saying that the situation in the north was about to change, and that someone had invited him to serve as the director of the construction department, etc. Unexpectedly, he actually joined Yin Rugeng in rebelling and harming the country. When the news spread, people from all walks of life in politics, education, military, and police here were filled with indignation. Yesterday, colleagues in the Jiangsu educational community and the teachers and staff of the Provincial Zhenjiang Teachers' School issued a declaration, unanimously denouncing him and asking the people of the country to abandon this kind of degenerate element. The provincial government, considering Wang's obvious rebellious actions, specifically brought it up at the Provincial Government Committee meeting, which resolved to dismiss him. As for the successor to the director of the Provincial Suzhou Library, the Education Department has already appointed Jiang Jinghuan to serve as the acting director. The details are as follows:

A Member of the Central Committee Issues a Statement

After learning of this news, the reporter immediately visited a member of the Central Committee in the province and asked for his thoughts on Wang Delin's rebellion and betrayal of the country. He was kind enough to issue the following statement, which roughly said: "In recent years, the country has been beset with difficulties, and worries and hardships have been frequent. We rely on the unity of the people across the country to overcome the difficulties together. Everyone with a sense of national pride understands this deeply. Hebei is a strategic area of paramount importance. People from all walks of life are able to persevere and maintain their position, striving to provide support. Any disturbance will affect the safety and security of the region. Especially for civil servants, they have specific duties and responsibilities, and should inspire their conscience and devote their wisdom to loyalty, working together to defend the country. However, Yin Rugeng, the Administrative Commissioner of the Luan-Yu District of Hebei Province, arbitrarily declared on the 25th of this month the establishment of the so-called Eastern Hebei Anti-Communist Committee, colluding with traitors and attempting to betray the country, which is already a heinous crime and an abandonment of humanity. Unexpectedly, Wang Delin, as a high-ranking member of the educational community, was actually bewitched by him and joined the rebellion, blinded by profit and abandoned by the people of the country. We predict that the false organization of Yin and other rebels who betray the people and the country will soon be eliminated. Now, the Central National Government has issued a clear order to arrest the rebel Yin Rugeng and ordered the Hebei Provincial Government to handle it directly, quickly curbing the unrest. Wang Delin will regret it at that time," he said.

Jiangsu Education Community Issues a Declaration Denouncing Him

Since the news of Wang Delin, Director of the Provincial Suzhou Library, joining the rebellion and betraying the country spread, people from all walks of life here have been extremely indignant. The education community, in particular, believes it is unfortunate that such a degenerate element has emerged and issued a declaration denouncing him, asking the people of the country to abandon him. The declaration of the teachers and staff of the Zhenjiang Teachers' School is as follows: "The newspaper reported on November 26 that Wang Xiacai participated in the activities of the puppet Eastern Hebei Anti-Communist Autonomous Organization and represented the traitor Yin in external negotiations, which is clearly an act of rebellion. Wang Xiacai has served in Suzhou for many years and is currently the director of the Suzhou Library. He secretly left his post and participated in conspiracies. He is greedy for wealth and endangers the country. He is a moth in our education community. We are willing to abandon him together with the people of the country. This is our declaration."

Jiang Jinghuan Succeeds as Director

The Jiangsu Education Department immediately selected Jiang Jinghuan, the director of the promotion department of the library, to fill the vacancy of director of the Suzhou Library. A special telegram was sent to summon Jiang to the province to receive instructions from the department and to return to the library immediately to take over and assume his duties properly. Jiang's brief resume is as follows: Jiang Jinghuan, 39 years old, a native of Wuxian County, graduated from the National Nanjing Higher Normal School. He has served as a teacher at the Suzhou Art Vocational School, an administrator at the Jiangsu Official Book Printing Office, a standing committee member of the Fourth District Local Education Research Association of the Central University, a lecturer in library science, an executive committee member of the All-Jiangsu Library Association to the China National Library Association, and the director of general affairs of this library. He has continued to hold his position for 14 years since July of the 11th year of the Republic.

Wang Delin's Past Teaching Positions

Wang Delin, style name Xiacai, 38 years old, a native of Wuxing, Zhejiang Province, a Bachelor of Arts from the National Peking University, has served as the director of academic affairs at the Jiangsu Private Women's Vocational Middle School, the Jiangsu Provincial Women's Second Normal School, the provost of the Shanghai Wenzhi University, the president of the Southern University General Association, a professor at the Hubei College of Political Science and Law, the principal of the Jiangsu Provincial Huaiyin Middle School, an editor at the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, a professor at the Beiping Sino-French University, and the director of the Jiangsu Provincial Suzhou Library. Now, out of greed for wealth, he secretly left his post and joined the rebellion, which is intolerable by the laws of the country, abandoned by the people of the country, and an abandonment of humanity. It is truly lamentable. (29th)

Hangzhou Air Defense Drill; Military and Police on High Alert, Resembling a State of War 87

Hangzhou Correspondence: After receiving orders to prepare for the joint air defense drill in Beijing, Zhenjiang, and Hangzhou, the Hangzhou Municipality immediately instructed its various units to actively prepare and established a temporary air defense drill headquarters, with Zhou Zhirou as commander, Xuan Tiewu as deputy commander, and Jiang Jianren as chief of staff. It also set up four sections and one committee, mobilizing personnel from various agencies to plan and prepare everything. It began yesterday (the 28th). The central government specially sent Vice Chief of Staff Xiong Bin to Hangzhou to serve as the air defense supervisor and invited Huang Shaohong to serve as the chief judge. Officials from various agencies were invited to serve as judges, inspectors, and instructors. At 7:20 a.m. yesterday, a simulated enemy aircraft was spotted in the airspace over the lower reaches of the Qiantang River, flying from east to west. At 8:00 a.m., another enemy aircraft was spotted, and enemy aircraft were also spotted in Haiyan County. After receiving the report, the air defense authorities knew that multiple enemy aircraft were flying to Hangzhou to attack. They immediately dispatched machine gun teams and rescue teams to set off in different directions, and urgently notified the citizens to act in accordance with the regulations. Shops immediately ceased operations and traffic control was implemented, cutting off traffic to prevent danger. Later, it was reported that the enemy fleet had arrived in the coastal area and appeared to be attacking Hangzhou. Aircraft were dispatched to Hangzhou Bay for reconnaissance. At 8:00 a.m., the aircraft reported by radio that a simulated enemy fleet was anchored at a certain location. Defense aircraft were dispatched to bomb it, destroying an enemy aircraft carrier. At 10:40 a.m., it was learned that the enemy aircraft had no intention of attacking Hangzhou, and the alert was lifted. At 2:00 p.m., the air defense observation post reported that 11 enemy aircraft were attacking Hangzhou from Nanjing. Our side immediately dispatched a defensive flight team to intercept them. Traffic control was re-implemented in the urban area, shops immediately closed their doors, and pedestrians were advised by the police to enter shelters for refuge. All kinds of vehicles retreated into secluded streets and alleys. The bustling commercial areas were as quiet as late at night, as if they had fallen into a state of war. At 2:15 p.m., when our fighter planes flew to the airspace over Haining, they encountered enemy aircraft and engaged in fierce combat. At that time, six enemy aircraft, divided into two teams, attempted to invade Jianqiao along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road, but due to the strict defense of our army, they changed direction and attacked Hangzhou. Our side immediately issued an emergency alarm and immediately dispatched aircraft to release smoke screens, covering various important transportation agencies and obscuring the enemy aircraft's targets. Flight teams were also dispatched to intercept them. Six enemy aircraft, divided into two teams in a character formation, four fighters and two bombers, flew in the city's airspace and dropped dozens of incendiary bombs, poison gas bombs, and bombs on our city railway station, Zhakou, Genshanmen, Gongchenqiao, Wulinmen, Security Office, telephone bureau, etc. A section of civilian housing in Meidong Gaoqiao near the city station caught fire. At 3:37 p.m., it was reported that the Zhakou Railway Factory was also bombed and caught fire. The nearby provincial defense team and Yilong rushed to put out the fire. Four men and women on the upper floors of a civilian house at the railway station were unable to escape. Two were rescued by the fire brigade with ladders, and two jumped out of the window, suffering minor injuries. They were taken to a temporary hospital for treatment by the rescue team. The remaining fire was also extinguished. Some of the onlookers were injured by poison gas and were also rescued by students from the Zhejiang Medical College, who were part of the rescue team. The performance was realistic and the results were excellent. Other damaged railway tracks, telephone lines, and water pipes were immediately repaired by the engineering team. At the same time, many reactionary elements who took the opportunity to cause trouble were captured and handed over to the military authorities for interrogation. The blackout, which began at 8:00 p.m., plunged the entire city into darkness. The military and police were on high alert, as if facing a formidable enemy. At around 9:00 p.m., the street lamp wire on Yingchai Road suddenly short-circuited, creating a dangerous situation, but it was calmly extinguished, fortunately without causing any disaster. However, due to the drizzling rain, the performance of dropping illuminating parachutes could not be held. The entire city was restored to light at 9:30 p.m.
