Local News

Chen Zhongbi Arrives in Shanghai to Negotiate Guangdong Provincial Construction Bonds; Pledge of 3 Million Yuan... Obtains Agreement from Three Banks 88

Central News Agency: The 5 million yuan Guangdong Provincial Construction Bonds of the 24th year of the Republic, passed by the Legislative Yuan, will be issued tomorrow (the 1st). Lin Yunhai, Chairman of Guangdong Province, has been discussing borrowing cash with banking circles in Shanghai and there are already signs of progress. He telegraphed Chen Zhongbi, President of the Guangzhou Municipal Bank, to come to Shanghai for detailed discussions. Yesterday, the reporter interviewed Mr. Chen, who stated that he had already obtained the agreement of the Central Bank and other banks. The following is a record of his conversation:

Key Points of the Bond Regulations

The Guangdong Construction Bonds amount to 5 million yuan and are being issued with the assistance of the Central Government. The regulations were passed by the Legislative Yuan six months ago. The issuance date is December 1st, but due to procedural delays, it may be postponed to January of next year. The term of the bonds is set at five years, with full repayment by the end of November (or December) of the 29th year of the Republic. The principal and interest will be paid twice a year, at the end of May and November. The collateral for the bonds is all the assets of the province's [unclear] factory. The factory's total revenue last year was 2 million yuan, and it is expected to increase to 3 million yuan after full operation.

Mortgage Agreement Obtained

The bond certificates are currently being printed by the Commercial Press in Shanghai and will soon be completed. It is planned to mortgage 3 million yuan to the banking circles in Shanghai. Lin Yunhai has already discussed this with the banking circles in Shanghai and there are signs of progress. I (Chen Zhongbi said himself) took a flight here yesterday (the 28th) for detailed discussions. This morning (i.e., yesterday morning), I visited Vice President Chen Xing of the Central Bank, Manager Bei Songsun of the Shanghai branch of the Bank of China, and General Manager Tang Shoumin of the Bank of Communications. I have obtained their agreement and will have further discussions soon.

Designated Use of Bond Funds

According to Mr. Chen, the use of the bond funds is designated as part of the working capital for various factories run by the province. The factories that are currently in operation or being established include five sugar factories and one textile factory. The textile factory is divided into five parts: silk weaving, cotton weaving, hemp weaving, spinning, and silk fabric products. Its scale is very large. Other factories include a paper mill, a sulfuric acid plant, a cement plant, a fertilizer plant, a beverage plant, and a caustic soda plant, totaling six plants.

Striving for Thrift and Construction

Mr. Chen continued that the capital needed to establish the above-mentioned factories is more than 30 million yuan. Although the burden on the people of Guangdong Province is heavy, the government is also working hard to be thrifty. Therefore, the above-mentioned factories have been able to achieve success in a short period of two and a half years. There are also steel mills and hydropower plants currently under planning and construction. The former is estimated to require 32 million yuan, and the latter requires 38 million yuan, totaling 70 million yuan. Efforts will be made to tighten government expenses to engage in construction, he said.

Guangdong Province Succeeds in Sugar Cane Farmers' Loan, Totaling 1.4 Million Yuan 89

Feng Rui, Director of the Guangdong Agricultural and Forestry Bureau, and Zou Bingwen, Vice President of the Shanghai Bank, and Shen Shuyu, Director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, have successfully negotiated a loan for sugar cane farmers, totaling 1.4 million yuan. The Shanghai Bank and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau will each be responsible for half, with a term of one year and a monthly interest rate of eight percent. Panyu and Shunde counties are designated as the loan areas, and the loan is limited to fertilizer and sugar cane seeds. All the measures have been agreed upon, and Director Feng has returned to Guangdong from Shanghai.

Signing the Contract

The Shanghai Bank and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau will meet today to discuss the loan measures. It is reported that the original plan was for sugar cane farmers in Panyu and Shunde counties to organize sugar cane farmers' purchasing cooperatives, lend the funds to the cooperatives, and then distribute them to the farmers. Now, it is proposed to change the method and lend the funds directly to the sugar cane farmers, guaranteed by the Guangdong Provincial Government, because the sugar cane farmers in the area are very reliable. As for the loan contract, it will be telegraphed to Guangdong after today's meeting, and then formally signed by the Shanghai Bank branch and the Postal Savings and Remittance branch in Guangdong and the Guangdong Provincial Government.

Loan Date

Guangdong farmers plant sugar cane once a year, with the planting period around January and the harvest period around December. The loan date after the success of this loan will be from New Year's Day in the 25th year of the Republic until the farmers return the loan after the harvest. As for the 700,000 yuan loan that the Shanghai Bank independently lent to the sugar cane farmers in Panyu County at the end of last year, it has been decided that the borrowing farmers will directly return the loan to the bank starting in December.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Banqueted Lin Yunhai Last Night; Yu Zuoting and Wang Xi Gave Welcoming Speeches; Liu Jiwen Delivered a Speech Hoping for Commercial Liaison 90

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce welcomed Lin Yunhai, Chairman of the Guangdong Provincial Government, at the Chamber yesterday at 7:00 p.m.. Also present were Liang Zhihuai, Secretary of the Provincial Government, Liu Jiwen, Mayor of Guangzhou, Chen Yuanying, Director of the Guangdong Products Management Office, Chen Zhongbi, President of the Guangdong Municipal Bank, Kuang Songling, Secretary of the Guangdong Construction Department, and Huang Heli, Member of the Guangdong Provincial Party Committee. The hosts were Xu Jilong, Jin Runxiang, Chen Zheqing, Ke Ganchen, Zheng Zenan, Ma Shaoquan, Pan Xusheng, Chen Yizhou, Ma Jiliang, Hu Xiguo, Zheng Dengqing, Ge Jechen, Ye Yinshan, Fang Jiaobo, Pei Yunqing, Du Yuesheng, Luo Qinghua, Shen Tianxin, Wang Xiaolai, Advisor, and Chen Ziyi, Gu Xinyi, Lao Jingxiu, and others. Chairman Yu Zuoting delivered a welcoming speech, and Chairman Lin responded with a speech. Mayor Liu and others also delivered speeches. The details are as follows:

Welcoming Speech

Chairman Yu Zuoting said in his welcoming speech: "Chairman Lin of the Guangdong Provincial Government recently passed through Shanghai after attending the National Congress of Representatives. The business community of this city is able to admire his grace, which is a rare opportunity. Guangzhou and Shanghai are both the earliest commercial ports opened in our country, and Guangdong Province's new industry has flourished in recent years, increasing its close relationship with Shanghai. It allows each other to communicate and make up for each other's shortcomings in commerce. It is a new trend in the development of Shanghai-Guangdong commerce that is worthy of attention. Therefore, our Chamber represents the city's industrial and commercial circles at this time, with a simple wine, inviting you to stop by. It is to express our long-cherished admiration and give each other an opportunity to talk. We are fortunate to have you visit. In recent years, the central government has been determined to carry out construction, and Guangdong Province is one of the most diligent provinces in its implementation. As far as what is known to the people of Shanghai in recent years, such as sugar manufacturing, its products are sold in large quantities in Shanghai in addition to the province's own supply, which is enough to block some loopholes. This is a very gratifying thing in the call to revitalize domestic products. As the saying goes, the auxiliary cart depends on each other. In a country, it is like a family, and it is better to maintain each other. For example, if the products of Guangdong's sugar factories are only sold in this province, and no efforts are made to promote sales in other provinces and cities, its development will be limited. Also, regarding sugar cane planting loans, the financial circles in Shanghai also understand deeply that this move has a great relationship with the revitalization of domestic products, and they have wholeheartedly accepted it. In view of the above two things, the industrial and commercial circles in Shanghai have a common feeling today, that is, "From the production perspective, we can take each province's needs and strengths as a unit. From the sales perspective, from the tax perspective, we should take the entire territory as an economic unit, and it is not appropriate to divide the boundaries." The transit tariffs that our country has always set up, where the native products of this province are transported to another province, the customs must collect transit taxes, which is the most obstructive to the development of domestic products and does not conform to the tariff system of various countries. Therefore, the central government has resolutely decided to abolish it in the near future. The Ministry of Finance has repeatedly expressed this, and the National Government issued an explicit order several years ago to abolish the likin of the provinces, also in order to implement this policy. Today, there should be no more commodity taxes collected between provinces, and the meaning is clear. A few years ago, Guangdong Province had a proposal to collect protective taxes on goods from outside the province, which was exempted after the sincere request of the industrial and commercial circles in Shanghai, which proves that the Chamber's above-mentioned contributions have been understood by the authorities and officials in Guangdong, for which we would like to express our sincere gratitude at this gathering today. In recent years, the industrial and commercial circles in Shanghai have declined sharply, and the reason is that after the fall of the four northeastern provinces, North China has also experienced fluctuations, so the sales in the two places have been completely cut off, and one has been greatly reduced, resulting in today's incurable disease. Therefore, today's domestic market has been limited to the Yangtze River Basin and the Pearl River Basin. The Pearl River Basin, with its agricultural product taxes, miscellaneous taxes, and special taxes on reformed products from outside the province, which have been successively implemented after repeated appeals but have not been exempted, is also trapped in the difficulty of sales, with the risk of discounts and losses. Today, Shanghai merchants are in a four-sided predicament, and they have great expectations for your efforts to mediate. We look up to you as a guiding light, and we would like to take this opportunity to express our sincerity and offer our humble suggestions. If you are willing to adopt them, how fortunate we would be!"

Lin's Reply

Chairman Lin Yunhai of Guangdong Province replied, roughly saying: "I am very grateful for the warm reception from your Chamber during this trip to Shanghai. I am also very grateful for the sincere help of the members of your Chamber. Shanghai is the first commercial port in our country and the center of commerce in the country. It has been affected by the unprosperous atmosphere in recent years, so that it is not as good as before, but as long as the people and the government work together, there is hope for recovery and prosperity. Our country has a vast territory and a large population, and is rich in products. We should find ways to develop railways, highways, and water conservancy to facilitate transportation, so that the agricultural products of the countryside and the industrial products of the city can be exchanged with each other. For example, the raw materials and supplies for industry used to rely on foreign imports. In the future, we should use our country's agricultural raw materials to imitate foreign products to develop industry. At the same time, agriculture, industry, and mining should support each other and work hard. We should also develop our country's local sales, and there will inevitably be great results in the future. Although we are in this period of depression, we should not be discouraged, but continue to work hard to develop. I wish you all success."

Liu's Speech

Mayor Liu Jiwen of Guangzhou said in his speech: "Shanghai's commercial center is on the surface, and the city's commercial offices are all-encompassing and the best in the country. The Guangdong Chamber of Commerce is incomplete, so there is no connection with other places. In the future, chambers of commerce in various places should be connected with each other. For example, Japanese commercial liaisons in various markets in China, such as Shanghai, Hankou, Yichang, and Guangdong, have statistics on sales. If place B lacks goods, they will telegraph place A to supply them, and the adjustment is proper, which has taken away our market. There is no organization in our country, and we have lost contact, which has led to failure. Therefore, we should unite and connect and collect statistics in order to have a way. In view of this, Guangdong welcomes Shanghai business people to transport goods to Guangdong, and Guangdong transports goods to Shanghai. We will earnestly connect with each other to promote sales, and strive to win back the markets that have been taken away by foreigners." The gathering ended in joy at around 10:00 p.m.

Two Trade Associations Jointly Send Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Urging Implementation of Commercial Acceptance Drafts; Support for Mr. Luo Qinghua's Three Proposals; Request for Representatives to Expedite Rediscounting 93

After the Municipal Chamber of Commerce initiated the implementation of commercial acceptance drafts to improve the account sales system and increase payment instruments, various industries began to promote it in response to the ability of these drafts to improve the current credit system. However, the rediscounting system was not yet complete, hindering the full realization of its benefits. At a time when the government is implementing monetary system reforms, various industries are eager to actively promote these drafts to aid the government's industrial recovery. Previously, Mr. Luo Qinghua sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce proposing: (1) request the Central Bank to promptly formulate rediscounting measures in accordance with laws and regulations and handle rediscounting business; (2) request the banking and money industries associations to strongly support the promotion of acceptance drafts, and first handle acceptance and rediscounting business for the recognized small-amount loan fund; (3) request the Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee to list and disclose the names and amounts of small-amount loan banks and businesses that have pledged contributions and distribute them to various industry associations. Yesterday, the paper, dyeing and weaving, rubber, electrical machinery and silk weaving, knitting, electrical appliance, glass, biscuit and confectionery, silk and satin printing, canning, cotton cloth, and other trade associations jointly sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce supporting Mr. Luo's proposals and requesting the dispatch of representatives to expedite rediscounting to facilitate circulation. The original letter from the various industry associations is recorded below:

Letter from Paper Industry, etc.

Respected Sirs, Since the outflow of silver from Shanghai last year, credit has tightened, industry and commerce have been in distress, and economic panic has prevailed, the severity of the situation is unprecedented. Your esteemed association has led merchants and gathered experts to jointly study and devise remedial measures. As a result, Mr. Luo Qinghua's proposal for the promotion of commercial acceptance drafts was adopted. The associations, recognizing that the current economic tsunami cannot be contained in a short period, and that the stagnation of account receivables in various industries needs to be improved, feel that commercial acceptance drafts are more flexible and convertible than the account sales system. On the one hand, they can increase payment instruments. Therefore, the associations have followed your esteemed association in unanimously promoting them. Unfortunately, the assistance from various parties is limited by their strength, resulting in the failure to fully realize the benefits of the promotion. Several weeks ago, your esteemed association sent a letter to the Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee, proposing to allocate three million yuan from the small-amount loans pledged by banks and businesses as an acceptance rediscounting fund, and the Loan Committee has accepted your esteemed association's proposal and decided to proceed accordingly. We believe that with the fund in place, implementation can proceed without worry. We hope that the financial industry can follow this lead and promote it together, and that the Central Bank will handle rediscounting in accordance with the law, so that payment instruments can be increased and industry and commerce can have hope of recovery. However, a long time has passed and it has not been implemented. Industry and commerce are eagerly waiting, like waiting for the new year. The three points mentioned in Mr. Luo Qinghua's letter to your esteemed association reported the other day are what the associations wanted to say and are indeed essential for rescuing industry and commerce and promoting recovery. As for the request for the Central Bank to handle rediscounting, we have heard that your esteemed association plans to dispatch representatives, together with the chairmen of the banking and money industries associations, to request the financial authorities to order its implementation. However, many days have passed, the end of the year is approaching, and industry and commerce are in greater need of assistance than in the past. The circulation of bills is still a pie in the sky. Therefore, the associations, in addition to unanimously supporting Mr. Luo Qinghua's three proposals, also request your esteemed association to check the previous proposal, dispatch representatives, and request the Central Bank to quickly formulate rediscounting measures to facilitate circulation and maintain industry. We are eagerly awaiting your instructions. This is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Letter from Cotton Cloth Industry

Respected Sirs, We believe that to promote the recovery of industry and commerce, it is necessary to increase credit instruments first. The implementation of acceptance bills has been the unanimous desire of various industries and is recognized worldwide. Unfortunately, although the banking industry and the Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee had previously planned to implement acceptance bills, they have not been implemented to date. The commercial acceptance drafts promoted by various associations have not achieved significant results due to the failure to resolve the rediscounting issue. Therefore, although we advocate relief day and night, the lack of instruments remains the same, and the decline of the market remains the same. Now, fortunately, the government is implementing a currency management policy, and the Central, China, and Communications Banks have formed a unified entity. Financial institutions are becoming increasingly consolidated. The issue of rediscounting should no longer be a concern. If we can take this opportunity to promote acceptance bills to increase credit instruments, it will undoubtedly benefit the recovery of industry and commerce. Our association, witnessing the current difficulties, cannot remain silent. Therefore, we are sending this special letter, respectfully hoping that your esteemed association will present it to the Ministry of Finance as soon as possible, forwarding it to the Central Bank, and promptly formulate rediscounting measures in accordance with the law and handle rediscounting business. One hundred, please also send separate letters to the banking and money industries associations and the Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee, urging them to handle bank acceptance bills to replace mortgage loans and promote commercial acceptance drafts to replace credit loans, in order to save the critical situation and benefit industry and commerce. We eagerly await your instructions with the utmost anticipation. This is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Director Cai Explains Improvement of Real Estate Mortgage Issues 96

The Shanghai-based North China Daily News recently commented on the "Shanghai Real Estate Mortgage Improvement Issues" proposed by Director Cai Zengji of the Land Bureau. Yesterday, Director Cai published an explanation of the issues in the newspaper, which is translated as follows:

Necessity of Improving Mortgaged Real Estate

Shanghai's land issues have special and distorted characteristics. To resolve the proposed land reform, it is necessary to briefly describe the complexity and shortcomings of the current land system so that society can understand the necessity of improving the current mortgaged real estate system.

弊弊 in Tao Deed Registration Procedures

Even the most common Tao deeds are not immune to malpractices. A Tao deed is a lease registered in the name of a foreigner at the consulate. Although the registered owner of this type of land is a foreigner, most of them are acting as trustees on behalf of the original owner. The original owner is then granted a Tao deed and a trust deed by the registered owner. This system is unique to China and is not found elsewhere. In land transfers, registered owners have been known to take the opportunity to exchange for new deeds and give them to another new owner without the original owner's knowledge. When disputes arise, the court often rules that the property belongs to the original owner, and the new owner is a person who has violated land rights.

Cunning People Often Use Substitute Mortgages

In addition, there are also registered owners who often do not know the address of the original owner and cannot communicate with them, and have to bear various taxes on their behalf. Therefore, the relationship between the registered owner and the original owner is unsatisfactory. In addition, registered owners often do not have complete records of the original owner's credentials. For example, the original owner only stamps a seal and considers it a receipt, without signing it in addition to the seal. If the person is illiterate, they do not add a fingerprint as proof. Due to these incomplete records and the general public's lack of understanding of the legal procedures and customs of real estate, cunning people often use illegal methods to obtain the legal owner's land deed, trust deed, and even seal to implement a mortgage. The lender, in good faith, is unaware of the situation and believes that the mortgage is legal. However, the loan is actually given to a person who has stolen the deed, and there is no legal protection.

Only Registration Can Protect Rights

In summary, due to the complex issues and shortcomings of land, it is known that land mortgages cannot provide legal protection to the mortgagee and mortgagor without registration with the Land Bureau. When land is registered, the Land Bureau carefully considers the land deed and property rights. If the land deed is approved for registration, it proves that the owner is the legal owner. When the lender mortgages the loan, they also know that the person they are transacting with is the legal owner. Even if cunning people want to exploit the situation, they will find it difficult. Therefore, mortgage registration is a necessary procedure to protect the rights of the people.

Fair Handling Depends on the Courts

As for the fair protection of the interests of both the mortgagor and the mortgagee, the local court should be the organ for handling such lawsuits. Regarding this point, a world-renowned financier also expressed dissent and stated that "if appeals can be executed in the court, it is not without obstacles to issuing the suggestion." However, given the special circumstances of land in Shanghai, there is no sufficient reason to directly abolish court appeals. However, if the registration system can be implemented, the current shortcomings and malpractices will naturally be eliminated, and although appeals cannot be completely eliminated, they should be reduced. According to the Land Law, before the establishment of a land court, the local court will only temporarily handle special mortgage cases that cannot be cleared by administrative power through registration.

Restrictions on Auction Rules

As for the rule that requires the mortgagee to provide security before conducting a public auction, it only applies to protect the rights of the legal owner when the above-mentioned disputes occur. However, in practice, it is not lightly cited unless the Director of the Land Bureau determines that the mortgagee has sufficient legal evidence to win the case.

Torrens System Can Be Adopted

The Torrens system is the most complete land system. However, even in this system, it is unavoidable to rely on the protection of the court to enforce mortgage rights. According to the current Torrens system in the United States, all transfers, such as mortgages and leases, must be recorded in the land certificate. All deeds are guaranteed by the government, and any transfer of property must be certified by a person designated by the government. As for mortgaged property, most of it is prepared by a lawyer on behalf of the mortgagee, and the mortgagor signs and acknowledges the fulfillment of the conditions proposed by the mortgagee before a notary public. If the mortgagor fails to fulfill the conditions, the mortgagee will take legal action to enforce the mortgage and may apply to the land court for enforcement. After the legally stipulated period expires, usually about thirty days, it will be auctioned off. This simple system is commendable and can be used as a reference for reforming the land system.

Welcome Suggestions and Proposals from All Sectors

The situation of the land system in Shanghai needs to be studied from all aspects. Fundamental reform cannot be achieved without the joint assistance and planning of all relevant groups, such as the Real Estate Association, real estate companies, consulate registration departments, the press, the legal profession, the banking industry, and various experts. All suggestions related to solving land problems are welcome, and it is hoped that society will correct its shortcomings.

Bullet Removed from President Wang's Back Yesterday; Temporarily Suspended Due to Physical Weakness; Surgery to Resume After Several Days of Rest 98

According to the Central News Agency, after an examination by doctors Niu Huilin, Niu Huisheng, and Noel, it was deemed necessary to remove the bullet from President Wang's back. At about 10:00 AM yesterday, the doctors gathered at Wang's residence, and at 11:30 AM, they began the surgery. Doctors Niu Huilin and Niu Huisheng performed the incision, and Doctor Noel monitored the pulse and physical health. After the incision, it was discovered that the bullet was tightly lodged between the ribs, making it difficult to remove. After an hour and a half, the bullet was finally removed from the ribs, but it was still in the muscle and had not been removed. Because too much time had passed, President Wang's physical strength gradually weakened, so the doctors decided to temporarily suspend the surgery and plan to continue the surgery after resting for a few days and regaining some strength. According to the doctors, now that the bullet has been removed from the ribs, the next removal will be easier.

Now, the Fujian Provincial Government's Ministry of Finance's No. 3948 of November 7, 1935, replies, stating briefly that the Shanghai Special Zone Chamber of Commerce had previously submitted a report, and the Shun Chang County Magistrate had been ordered to investigate and abolish it. Correspondingly, we reply for your information. After investigation, it has been abolished by the province. The Ministry of Finance is grateful. (National News Agency)

Date for Changing Account Books and Affixing Stamps Is Established; National Federation of Commerce Sends Telegram Requesting Maintenance 106

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce separately telegraphed the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry yesterday: To the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing, Recently, a telegram from the Beijing Municipal Chamber of Commerce opened, stating that Article 10 of the Implementation Rules of the Stamp Tax Law stipulates that all temporary examples of stamp tax and separate regulations of various provinces, as well as all established cases approved by the Ministry of Finance in the past to exempt, postpone, or reduce stamp tax, shall be abolished. It is not clearly stipulated whether the established case that has been implemented for many years of changing new account books and affixing new stamps during the period from February 1st to 15th is also included in the abolition. This association is particularly panicked because merchants are accustomed to changing new account books after February 1st. If it is suddenly changed to January 1st, there will be many difficulties in practice. We should understand the actual situation and allow the national order to apply to the period from March 1st to 15th for the replacement of account books and the affixing of new stamps, except for those that apply to the accounting year. We earnestly request that your esteemed association immediately submit a flying report and unanimously appeal for the rapid issuance of orders and forward them to the judicial organs for investigation to avoid accidents. Please approve and order compliance, and forward them to the Legislative and Judicial Yuans to order compliance to avoid disputes. We pray that the Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Lin Kanghou, will solemnly print.

From Wusong to Yaogangzui, Light Buoys Replace Unlit Buoys 110

The Maritime Department of the Office of the Inspector General of Customs issued an announcement yesterday stating that the unlit buoys in the Yangtze River from Wusong to Yaogangzui under the jurisdiction of the Jianghai Customs should be removed and replaced with light buoys to facilitate nighttime navigation. All merchants and others are hereby notified of the removal and replacement of the buoys and the dates thereof. Details are as follows: A. Dates and circumstances of buoy removal and replacement: (1) It is expected that around December 17 of this year, the east entrance buoy of the Baimaosha South Channel, the upper buoy of the east corner of Baimaosha, the south buoy of the Baimaosha South Channel, and the west entrance buoy of the Baimaosha South Channel will be replaced with gas light buoys. Each of these light buoys is 10 feet in diameter and decorated in black. The lower buoy of the east corner of Baimaosha and the south buoy of the Baimaosha South Coast will also be replaced with the same gas light buoys, but decorated in red. (2) It is expected that around November 20 of this year, the Baimao River buoy, the south entrance buoy of the Tongzhou Channel, the Xu Liujingzui buoy, the east buoy of the Tongzhou Channel, the dangerous buoy of the Tongzhou Channel, and the turning buoy of the Tongzhou Channel will all be replaced with gas light buoys. Each of these light buoys is 10 feet in diameter and decorated in black. (3) All of the above light buoys are equipped with alternating flashing white lights, flashing once every eight seconds, with each flash lasting four seconds. B. Related charts: Maritime Department of the Republic of China Navy Chart Nos. 141 and 142. November 27, 1935, Maritime Engineering Department Patrol Engineer Kanais.

Tax Evasion and Smuggling of Salt Case: Verdict Pending 112

On September 17th of this year, the salt affairs tax police of the five counties of Suzhou discovered a ship evading salt tax near the Kaigangkou area of Haimen County. The ship was carrying over 10,000 dan of smuggled salt. At that time, salt smugglers Yang Guangyou (age 20, from Yancheng) and Huang Shanqing (age 34, from Haimen) were arrested and sent to the local court's prosecutor's office for interrogation and detention. Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu conducted a clear investigation and prosecuted the case to the criminal court under Article 1, Article 2, Paragraph 1, Item 3 of the Private Salt Act. Yesterday at 10 AM, Criminal Court President Cai Dingcheng specially opened the third courtroom for the trial. After the judge took his seat, he ordered the detained Yang Guangyou and Huang Shanqing to be brought forward. The defendants confessed that the loading and transportation of smuggled salt was done by the shipowner Yang Si and merchant Hu Youhong. They claimed to be ship crew members and only knew how to operate the ship, knowing nothing else, and asked for leniency. The judge, upon hearing the confession, stated that the case was already clear and invited Prosecutor Tang to the court to present his opinion. Finally, lawyer Zhou Yu was appointed to defend for a long time. The judge considered the case closed and scheduled a verdict. The two defendants were returned to custody.

Robbery at Guohua Cloth Factory in Dongjiadu, Pudong: Six Robbers with Local Accents 113

At 3:45 PM yesterday, six robbers suddenly entered the Guohua Weaving Factory at No. 10 Dongranfang Lane, Dongjiadu, South Shanghai. They first cut the telephone line to prevent any alarm. One robber stood guard outside, while three robbers pulled out guns, drove the workers into another room, and forced the manager, Qiu Shude, to hand over the keys. They robbed 79 yuan in banknotes, 6 US dollars, 66 cents in small coins, and 4,000 copper coins from the safe. They also searched the employees, stealing a silver watch, a gold ring, and clothing, before fleeing. Afterwards, the owner reported the incident to the Dongjiadu Police Station, requesting an investigation. It was determined that the six robbers were around 20 to 30 years old and spoke with local accents. One robber was wearing a dark-colored long robe and a black felt hat, while the other five were wearing blue cloth shirts and trousers, resembling workers. After receiving the report, the police station immediately dispatched detectives to arrest the suspects.

Foreign Monk Sues Russian Newspaper: Continued Trial, Court Advises Reconciliation 119

The Buddhist foreign monk Zhao Kong Seng sued the Russian-language "Chai La Wan Bao" at No. 77 Xiafei Road because the newspaper published an article on August 3rd of this year about Trebich Lincoln (translated sound, Zhao Kong's original name) inciting the situation in the Far East, supplying Abyssinia with weapons, and serving as a military detective. After Zhao Kong read it, he believed that the newspaper published the article and spread the words without reason, defaming him. He specifically hired Russian lawyer Yin Shengmin as his agent and submitted a lawsuit to the Second Special Court's Criminal Court, accusing the publisher of Chai La Wan Bao, Lin Biqi, and the editor, Weis, of violating Article 31 of the Criminal Law (defamation) and requesting an investigation. He also filed a civil lawsuit to recover 10,000 yuan in damages. The case had been summoned once, but the parties involved did not arrive, and the court ordered a rescheduling. This newspaper reported the details. Yesterday, the plaintiff and two French disciples, as well as the entrusted agents Lin Yingqing and Yin Shengmin, arrived in court. The defendants also arrived with their defense lawyer Jiang Guofang. At 10:20 AM, Judge Sun Penghang continued to hear the case in the Criminal Court. First, the plaintiff's agent, lawyer Yin Shengmin, stated in court that many newspapers had published that the plaintiff was a "strange talent," and requested the court to order reporters not to use the word "strange" again. The judge ruled that the court had no right to interfere with the freedom of speech of newspapers. If the plaintiff believed it was defamation, he could file a lawsuit. The court then questioned both parties' age, origin, occupation, and address. The plaintiff spoke French and translated his testimony. He was 57 years old, Hungarian, stateless, and lived at No. 12 Gongguan Road. His original name was Trebich Lincoln. The defendants spoke in Russian. Lin Biqi stated that he was 34 years old, a White Russian, and the publisher of Chai La Wan Bao, living at No. 403 Yarbei Road. Weis stated that he was 35 years old, a White Russian, and the chief writer of Chai La Wan Bao, living at No. 764 Pushi Road. At this point, the judge ordered the plaintiff to state the purpose of the lawsuit. He claimed that he requested the court to uphold justice and the protection of the law. Chai La Wan Bao published news that I was selling weapons, which damaged my reputation. But since I was born, I have never done such a thing, it's all rumors. The rest of the words are stated by my agent lawyer. Questioned the defendant Lin Bishi, I am the publisher of Chai La newspaper, the words recorded on the newspaper are all managed by the chief writer. Weis said that the words published in the newspaper were my responsibility for the description of the plaintiff Lincoln, transferred from the Latvia Today newspaper (according to the early newspaper) reprint, the original text is also in Russian, published as it is, followed by a few sentences, the officer asked The Latvia Today newspaper presented today only has empty frames and titles, where is the original text? Why didn't you indicate that it was a reprint? Wei Gong's newspaper clippings were burned after two months of storage because there was no place to store them, so it is not necessary to explain where the news came from. It has been stated that it came from European newspapers, the officer then ordered that the case could be rescheduled, and the original newspaper must be produced as evidence. The current publication is not enough to prove it. I hope the defendant can find a way to prove it. The defendant's lawyer rose up and said that the defendant has written to Harbin to find this newspaper, but I am afraid that it will be difficult to do it after a long time. The plaintiff's means are very spicy, and the defendant wants to buy a story self-described by modern spies published by the British Holysheng Bookstore, which the plaintiff admits to be a spy, and it is impossible to buy this book in the store. After thinking of various methods, I just bought it. The defendant published various things about the plaintiff in many European newspapers and the Shanghai Times, such as being arrested. The news was not reprinted, which is enough to prove that Po Gao had no malice, and according to the publication law, he can write a letter to correct it, etc. The court then advised both parties that this case is a crime of accusation, and reconciliation can be carried out during the political period. He then ordered a retrial to be scheduled, and announced the adjournment.

Rickshaw Trade Association Opposes Vehicle Committee's Arbitrary Fines 122

The Special District Rickshaw Trade Association recently reported that rickshaw pullers reported that the vehicle committee's vehicle owners had overcharged rickshaw rentals, and the vehicle committee arbitrarily fined and detained licenses. Yesterday, a letter was sent to the vehicle committee, requesting leniency. The original letter said: "Dear Sirs, we have recently received letters from vehicle owners Yu Hengzu, Wang Shengji, Lu Jingchang, Cai Hengxing, Jiang Caichen, Chen Wusheng, Zhang Tongxing, Zhong Kuanzha, Li Yousheng, Lu Genquan, Lu Xieikun, Zhou Zhiyun, Fang Dengfu, Liji, etc. The general idea is that the Public Works Department's vehicle committee, based on the rickshaw pullers' untruthful reports, accused them of overcharging rickshaw rentals, and fined them as much as 4 to 10 yuan per vehicle or detained their licenses for 7 days to 1 month, regardless of whether it is true or false, there must be a subpoena to those that are accused, there must be a fine to those that are summoned. At this time when vehicles are gradually being replaced and vehicle materials are becoming more and more expensive, the losses and hardships of vehicle owners are already unbearable. If they are fined innocently again, they will inevitably be on the verge of desperation. Please send representatives to negotiate on behalf of them, so as to avoid oppression, etc. According to this, the rickshaw rental fee, together with the mutual aid association fee collected on behalf, was originally set at 8 jiao and 5 fen of silver dollars per day. Later, because the rickshaw pullers did not have silver dollars to pay the rent, it was changed to 12 jiao of small silver coins per day, which was a fact. Since the promulgation of our country's new currency system, the letter from your association has been received, stating that 8 jiao and 5 fen of silver dollars should still be charged per day. We immediately notified all vehicle owners to follow the rules consistently. Unexpectedly, a few rickshaw pullers suddenly reported that the vehicle owners had overcharged rickshaw rentals, resulting in repeated fines. However, the vehicle owners all denied it, causing many disputes. We believe that these matters, whether true or not, should be handled leniently by your association first to avoid fines. In the future, we will definitely abide by the agreed rental fee consistently, without any deviation. Therefore, we are writing this letter to request your association to allow the withdrawal of all the orders for fines or license detentions for the rickshaw pullers' reports of overcharging rickshaw rentals, in order to show leniency and avoid disturbances. This is what we earnestly pray for."

Swindling a Woman of a Large Sum of Money, Claiming to Smuggle Silver Dollars, Exposed: Fabricating News of Bank Instability, Collateralizing Deposits: Zhou Wenkui Fled for Days, Arrest Pending 123

Sun Shiyu, who resided at No. 38 Taiping Lane, Suzhou, had a fixed deposit of 10,000 yuan in the Mainland Bank on Jiuzhou Road in Shanghai. Recently, Sun went to Dongtai County in Jiangbei for business. His wife and niece, Ma Yuying, were at home. On the 3rd of this month, Sun's friends, Zhou Wenkui and Jing Riru, employees of the Commercial Bank of China's branch on Aidoa Road in Shanghai, suddenly arrived at Sun's residence in Suzhou. They told Sun's wife that there was news of instability at the Mainland Bank. Knowing that Sun had a deposit there, they came specifically to inform her. However, the deposit was fixed-term and could not be withdrawn immediately. The only option was to pledge the deposit slip to the bank for a loan. Sun's wife believed it was true and, after obtaining her husband's consent via long-distance telephone, sent her niece, Ma Yuying, to Shanghai with Zhou and Jing. On the 6th, they pledged the deposit slip to the Mainland Bank and obtained 9,000 yuan in legal tender. In addition to Jing Riru acting as a witness, Zhou Wenkui also persuaded Wu Yaqin, the manager of the Commercial Bank of China's Nanshi branch, to guarantee the pledge. After the pledge was made, Zhou immediately suggested that the 9,000 yuan be deposited into the Bank of China's Hongkou branch under the name of Sun Shiyu. He then sent the deposit book to Sun's home. Later, Sun's wife received a phone call from her husband, instructing her to withdraw the money. Sun's wife then wrote a check, entrusting Zhou and others to withdraw the money and remit it to Suzhou. However, Zhou disappeared without a trace. On the 16th, Sun suddenly received a letter from Zhou from Ningbo, stating that the money had been used to smuggle silver dollars to Dalian, but the matter was exposed midway, so he could only slowly find a way to return it. After receiving the letter, Sun rushed to Shanghai and inquired at the Bank of China's Hongkou branch. He learned that 8,960 yuan had been withdrawn from the 9,000 yuan, leaving only 38 yuan and 2 jiao. After careful consideration, Sun felt that Zhou and Jing were highly suspicious and had engaged in a joint fraudulent act. He arrested Jing and handed him over to the General Police Station the day before yesterday. After investigation by Chinese detective Yang Peisheng, Jing was detained, and a search for Zhou Wenkui was launched, but he had already fled without a trace. Yesterday morning, Jing Riru was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu explained the situation, stating that Jing was highly suspected and requested permission to detain him for detailed investigation. Then, Ma Yuying recounted the details of the pledge. Judge Huang Risheng asked Jing about his age and origin. He stated that he was 26 years old, from Shaoxing, and resided at No. 3, Fudeli, Chengdu Road, working as an employee at the Commercial Bank of China. Judge Huang Risheng then questioned

the actual situation, and then ordered that Jing Riru should be allowed to be detained.

Search Lasts Three Hours: Nine Opium Pill Offenders Arrested: Shanghai Public Security Bureau Requests Transfer: Second Special Court to Rule Today 125

The Songhu Garrison Headquarters Military Law Department tried Cai Yulou, a drug trafficker presented by the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, and stated that he confessed that he had bought opium pills from Yuan Hongsheng, who resided at No. 12, Rihui Lane, Jinshenfu Road, French Concession. He immediately ordered the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to send a detective to report to the French police station at noon on the 25th of this month, requesting assistance in the arrest. Biye (translated sound), the Western detective of the French police station, and Zhu Zhihao, the Chinese detective, led the detectives Peng Zhengyou, Li Baochang, and Yang Weishan, etc., together with the detectives from the Public Security Bureau, went to No. 12, Rihui Lane, and arrested Yuan Hongsheng (36 years old, from Wuxi). Forty-five small packets of morphine and twenty-five small packets of red pills were found. At that time, Wang Tugen (33 years old, a coppersmith) and Zhang Dehui (31 years old, from Nantong), who lived with Yuan, were lying on the bed, smoking opium. Wang and Zhang, along with the smoking paraphernalia, opium pills, and morphine, were taken back to the police station. After interrogation, Yuan confessed that he had bought the morphine from Jiang Yongmei (30 years old, from Taizhou) on the upper floor of No. 569, Fada Road, and bought the red pills from Zhang Henxing (37 years old, from Hangzhou) at No. 10, Lane 150, Fuxu Road. After the detectives received the confession, they first went to No. 565, Fada Road, and arrested Jiang Yongmei. Jiang confessed that the morphine was hidden in the home of Cao Wangshi (29 years old), a fellow villager, at No. 9, Songbai Road, Limei Road. The detectives brought back Jiang and Cao Wangshi and her uncle Wu Jingwu (22 years old). After searching, nothing was found. After careful examination, they discovered a mechanism in the wardrobe on the back building that led to the wall. They then found a packet of morphine weighing about two taels and nearly 80 yuan in cash. They then went to No. 10, Lane 150, Fuxu Road, and arrested Zhang Genxing, who confessed that the red pills were hidden in the back building of No. 59, Beile Road. The detectives immediately went to the address and found eight bags of red pills, each containing 1,000 pills, and a full set of manufacturing equipment in a hidden compartment under the floor, packed in a white leather suitcase, as well as a wooden suitcase with a hidden compartment for transporting red pills. They arrested Wang Xiuying (21 years old), a young woman from Wuxi, and her lover, Yin Peiben (28 years old), both local, who were selling red pills. In total, nine men and women were arrested, and the search lasted three hours. The people and the evidence were taken to the police station and sent to the Second Special Court the next day for investigation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiong Huiping and Clerk Tao Zongkan came to the First Criminal Court for interrogation. Fei Xizhen, the lawyer of the Police Department, explained the case and stated that, except for Zhang Dehui, who was not prosecuted due to lack of evidence, the others were prosecuted according to Article 257 of the Criminal Law, and requested a trial according to the law. Then, Zhan Jifeng, the legal advisor of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, and the detectives filed a case, requesting permission to transfer Yuan Hongsheng, Wang Tugen, and Zhang Dehui back to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The court verified the report and then ordered the suspects to be interrogated separately. Yuan Hongsheng confessed to selling drugs in the concession and requested to be tried here, and did not want to be transferred. Wang Tugen confessed that he occasionally smoked opium because of illness and that he lived in the back parlor and was detained and had nothing to do with Yuan. Zhang Dehui confessed that he was in the kiln business and temporarily lived with his relative Yuan Hongsheng because he stopped working, and did not sell red pills with him. Cao Wangshi confessed that her husband used to sell morphine, but she did not sell it herself. Wang Xiuying confessed that the red pills were placed with her by a young sister to sell. The other suspects all denied their guilt. After verifying the confessions and after debate, the court announced the adjournment and scheduled the verdict for 2:00 p.m. on the 30th (today). The suspects were returned to custody. The seized opium pills, morphine, equipment, etc., were sent to the stolen goods warehouse.

South Railway Station Confiscates Narcotics Case: Key Suspect Ye Zicai Approved for Transfer and Handover. Suspect Ye is Wanted by Zhejiang Provincial Government for Other Cases 126

The Xida Xing Transportation Company at the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway South Station in this city, on the 23rd of this month at approximately 5:00 PM, received six sacks filled with goods from Wang Changgen, a Hangzhou resident. Wang claimed the sacks contained medicinal herbs destined for Lanxi, Zhejiang. However, suspicion arose when Wang was unable to provide a consignment note from the consigning company. Upon inspection, the sacks were found to contain foreign flour sacks filled with red pills, morphine powder, and other substances worth over ten thousand yuan. Wang Changgen was immediately detained, and the matter was reported to the Ximen Public Security Bureau. Furthermore, Hu Shimu (also known as Hu Zhirong), a resident of Taizhou, was apprehended outside the station and brought to the bureau. According to Hu's confession, Ye Zicai, a fellow villager residing at No. 21, Ren Shou Li, Wang Zhi Road, in the French Concession, had instructed him to have Wang deliver the goods to the station. Consequently, Shen Wenda, the captain of the Ximen Public Security Bureau's Detective Squad, led detectives, accompanied by Hu Shimu, to the French Concession Police Station to request assistance. They proceeded to No. 21, Ren Shou Li, Wang Zhi Road, where Ye Zicai was arrested and taken into custody at the police station. The following day, he was transferred to the Second Special District Court for interrogation. The Public Security Bureau, represented by legal advisor Zhan Jifeng, along with detectives from the Detective Squad, brought Wang and Hu to the court to await questioning. A request for transfer was made, but the French Concession Police Department, citing unfinished matters, requested a postponement. After deliberation, the retrial was rescheduled for yesterday. All details have been previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiong Huiping and clerk Tao Zongkan from the Second Special District Court arrived at the Criminal Division I courtroom. After establishing their positions and addresses, Fei Xizhen, the attorney from the Police Department, presented the Police Department's investigative process against the defendant. In court, addressing Ye, the judge stated, "The last time, you presented an alibi claiming you were at the home of Teng Zhonggao at No. 37, Ji Wu Fang, Ximen Road, at 11:00 AM on the 23rd. However, after sending police to investigate, it was reported that no such person exists there. Furthermore, if you did not hand the goods to Wang Changgen and Hu Shimu for transportation, why are their testimonies identical?" The defendant replied, "I did not entrust anyone to transport such goods. This is a great injustice. Moreover, I arrived in Shanghai on the night of the 22nd and went to the shipping company on the morning of the 23rd. At 11:00 AM, I was at the home of Teacher Teng, the wife of Teng Zhonggao, in Ji Wu Fang. I request a thorough investigation." Ge Zhiqin, the defendant's defense attorney, stated that the Teng surname mentioned by the defendant actually resides at No. 35, Ji Wu Fang, not No. 37, and requested a retrial and interrogation. The judge asked the defendant, "The Shanghai Public Security Bureau now wants to transfer you for questioning. Do you have any objections?" Ye replied, "I live in the French Concession and have not committed any crimes on Chinese soil. How can I be transferred?" At this point, Zhan Jifeng, the legal advisor representing the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, stood up and stated to the court, "Investigation reveals that the defendant Ye Zicai is not only involved in this crime. In November of last year, Wang Yonggui, arrested in Yiwu County, Zhejiang Province, for selling red pills, confessed to purchasing them from Ye Zicai. Simultaneously, it was discovered that red pill dealer Chen Wudi had remitted payment to Ye Zicai through the post office. Yiwu County requested the Zhejiang Provincial Government to issue a warrant for Ye Zicai's arrest, and the Provincial Government instructed the Shanghai Municipal Government to order the Public Security Bureau to arrest the defendant, but this was not achieved. We now have official documents from the Zhejiang Provincial Government as evidence, which we present for your inspection. Furthermore, as the government is currently strictly enforcing the ban on opium, the defendant's crime has been proven and does not conflict with the Concession Agreement. We request permission to transfer the defendant for investigation and prosecution." Shen Wenda, the captain of the Detective Squad, added, "After the Public Security Bureau received the official documents from the Zhejiang Provincial Government on November 13th of last year, I dispatched a squad leader to report to the French Concession Police Station, along with Chinese and foreign detectives, to arrest Ye at his home. Ye was not at home. According to his younger brother, Ye Mengxin, Ye Zicai had already been informed by fellow villagers, so he was not apprehended." The judge then asked Ye, "Did you know that the Zhejiang Provincial Government issued a warrant for your arrest?" He replied, "I have not committed any crime." The judge further asked, "Are you also known as Ye Tang?" He replied, "I do not have that name. I am also known as Ye Mengda." The judge asked, "Do you know Wang Xinquan?" He replied, "I do not know him." The court then ordered the Police Department's attorney and the defendant's attorney to debate the matter. Subsequently, the court ruled that Ye Zicai be handed over to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for transfer and investigation. Upon hearing the verdict, the defendant and his defense attorney declared in court that they would file an appeal.

Welcome to the Belgian Modern Art Exhibition - Xie Shou Kang 127

I.

Baron Guillaume de Giey, the Belgian Ambassador to China, places great importance on the development of cultural endeavors between China and Belgium. Last year, he organized a Belgian Modern Art Exhibition in Shanghai, and now he is organizing a similar exhibition in both Beijing and Shanghai. This year, the exhibition has been expanded, featuring over 130 works, which have been well-received in Beijing. The Shanghai exhibition will be held at Hamilton House, opening to the public today for one week. Ambassador de Giey's dedication and efforts in promoting cultural exchange between China and the East and West are commendable.

II.

Belgian painting is not only flourishing today, but the past Belgian school, the Flemish School, has a glorious history. Before introducing this exhibition, I will briefly outline its history to trace its origins.

Belgium's position in European painting history is extremely important. European painting only greatly developed after the application of oil-based pigments, and the masters of oil-based pigmentation were the Van Eyck brothers from Ghent, Belgium. At the same time, the Van Eyck brothers also incorporated sciences such as anatomy and perspective into painting. They, along with Weyden, Bouts, Memlings, and Goce, founded the Flemish School, the ancient Belgian school, in the fifteenth century AD.

The great achievement of the Van Eyck brothers' collaboration is a shrine, also known as the Polyptych. This shrine is composed of twenty wooden panels, with paintings on the surface of the wooden panels. There are two movable panels on each side, with paintings on both the front and back. The central structure of the shrine is the Adoration of the Mystic Lamb and the Fountain of Life. The upper level has seven panels, with the victorious Jesus in the center, flanked by the Virgin Mary and Saint John; further to the sides are angels playing music. Outside the angels, there are Adam on the right and Eve on the left. The lower-level panels depict Jesus' guards, righteous judges, hermits, farmers, and so on.

The faces, arms, clothing folds of the figures in the "Shrine," as well as the grass, trees, and fruits in the background, are all vividly detailed and seamless. The Shrine was completed on May 6, 1432 AD and was immediately displayed in the St. John's Church in Ghent, now the St. Bavo Cathedral. By the beginning of the 19th century, the shrine was incomplete, with several panels purchased by the Berlin Museum. In 1919, the Treaty of Versailles stipulated that they be returned to Belgium.

Weyden's works were very popular at the time, specializing in religious paintings. The solemnity, piety, and depth of his depictions of the Virgin Mary, Saint John, Magdalene, and the suffering of "those who buried Jesus" are unprecedented. Bouts' masterpiece is the Shrine of the Church of Louvain, whose theme is the "Last Supper." In addition, there are two "triptychs," one depicting the torture of Saint Erasmus and the other depicting the quartering of Saint Hippolytus. Bouts was particularly skilled at creating drawings with personality and colors with luster. Memling was a disciple of Weyden, whose technique was precise and gentle. His religious paintings had no striking colors or alarming emotions, only seeking serenity, integrity, compassion, and grace. In Belgian painting, the translucent shadows within the gauze layer and the subtle chiaroscuro on the faces of the figures are almost unbelievable. Memling is one of the greatest portrait painters in the history of painting, and most of his works are gathered in the St. John's Hospital in Bruges. As for Goce, although not a student of Weyden, he was greatly influenced by him. Scotland, Florence, Berlin, and Bruges all hold masterpieces of Goce. Among them, the "Adoration of the Shepherds" in Florence is the greatest. With its grand structure and realistic figures, Goce was truly a precursor to the 17th-century Flemish School.

In contrast to the early Flemish School, the Italian schools of the Renaissance flourished in the south. Southern painting was idealist, excelling in sketching and structure, specializing in historical sites, patterns, and nudes. Northern painting was realist, emphasizing color and light, specializing in portraits, landscapes, and still lifes. Although the two schools had different purposes and techniques, their brilliant achievements inspired countless later generations.

Subsequently, the Flemish School produced masters generation after generation, continuing without end. In the 16th century, Patinir created landscape paintings, Bosch created fantastical and demonic paintings, and Brueghel established a unique style, depicting peasant life and winter rural scenes with desolate and tragic emotions. At the time, his works were called "strange paintings." After the rise of populism in the 19th century, Bosch began to be admired by the world, recognized as the pioneer of peasant painters.

After Brueghel, Rubens brought the Flemish School to its culmination. Rubens encompassed everything, vividly and flawlessly depicting portraits, landscapes, animals, still lifes, religious stories, love stories, the gentry class, and folk tales. Artists of the time, and 18th-century English and French artists such as Reynolds, Gainsborough, and Watteau, all followed his example and were influenced by him. The number of works left behind by Rubens is unparalleled by any artist in history.

At the same time, Brouwer and Teniers specialized in small-scale paintings, creating extremely delicate, interesting, and well-organized paintings within a small format. Their success was comparable to Dutch small-scale painting, which is another characteristic of the Flemish School.

The 18th century was a period of decline for the Flemish School. Although there were many famous painters during this period, they could not be compared with the masters of the previous three centuries. After Belgium's independence in the 19th century, the Belgian school revived and flourished again, striving forward based on European trends to restore its inherent important position in the international arena. From 1830 to 1860, the Romantic school flourished, with the most famous painters being Lalaing and Wiertz, whose works were mostly focused on historical and symbolic paintings. From 1860 to 1880, the Realist school flourished, with the most famous painters being Groux, Stevens, and Meunier, whose specialty was depicting daily life. 1880 was the starting point of the Impressionist school. The Impressionists paid special attention to light and color, and Belgians had a great innate endowment for this, so their success was particularly great. Artists such as Glaus, Courtens, Frederic, Bastien, Ensor, Smith, Gilsoul, Laemans, and Wouters directly competed with the French masters of Impressionism's birthplace.

As for the Futurism, Dadaism, Cubism, Expressionism, Neo-Impressionism, and Neoclassical schools that emerged after the European War, Belgium also had them all. The first four schools were temporary trends with no achievements to speak of. The latter two schools continued to work hard, seeking light. However, in recent decades, most painters have not been bound by schools or followed existing styles, but have developed freely based on their individuality. Belgians are rich in artistic heredity and talent for color and form. Belgian painting has thus progressed and is truly inexhaustible!

III.

The modern Belgian school is the direct descendant of the ancient Flemish school. Although the styles of ancient and modern are different, their national characteristics are obviously present. There are many excellent works in this Belgian art exhibition. The style of the Flemish school can be seen at a glance. The exhibitors and their works are introduced separately below:

Among the great modern Belgian masters, the one who most admires our country's past excellent culture and is closest to our people is Mr. A. Bastien. Bastien is a painter who came from poverty, worked hard, and succeeded. He once served as the president of the Belgian Academy of Fine Arts. After the European War, he painted the Panorama de L'yser, which is 15 meters high and 150 meters long. This exhibition features a portrait of former Belgian King Albert I (No. 48). With concise brushstrokes, it fully reveals the King's heroic and indomitable spirit. There is also a flower and fruit painting with extremely simple brushstrokes and exceptionally magnificent colors.

Gilsoul is also one of the great modern masters, born in 1867. His "Village Front" (No. 65) has a quiet structure and skillful technique. "Old House" (No. 66) has the same style and is full of Flemish flavor.

Richir and Baes are both experts in women's portraits and are very popular with noble ladies. Richir's two women's portraits (No. 108 and No. 109) and Baes' two portraits of young girls (No. 9 and No. 10) are rendered in detail and are lifelike in form. Although their style is close to academic painting, their skill is unmatched.

Opsomer is the president of the Antwerp Academy of Fine Arts and enjoys a high reputation in the Belgian art world. Unfortunately, the color of his portrait (No. 100) in this exhibition is too yellow, perhaps due to preconceptions, and it is far from the success of his usual works. The second exhibit, "Flower," although elegant in color, seems cramped in structure.

Toussaint's "Flower" (No. 119), J. Albert's "Outskirts of Brussels" (No. 8), Clesse's "A Fisherman's Family" (No. 24), Creytens' landscapes (No. 34 and No. 35), Moitroux's portraits of women (No. 96 and No. 97), Thomas' "Flower Hat" (No. 118), Van de Leene's nude and Spanish woman (No. 120 and No. 121) all have skillful brushstrokes and exquisite colors, and can be called masterpieces.

As for Buisseret's "Contemplation" (No. 13) and "Peasant Woman" (No. 14), refined colors are added to extremely accurate sketches, and the folds of the clothes are extremely concise and have a modern flavor. This can be regarded as a representative work of the Neoclassical school.

Those who use knives instead of brushes are Crommelinck and Massonet. Crommelinck's "Peasant" and "Wind and Cloud" (No. 36 and No. 37), and Massonet's "Comedian Musician" and "Spaniard" (No. 90 and No. 91) all have a majestic momentum and profound meaning, and are quite unique.

Latinis' "Church Street" (No. 81) and "Country" (No. 82) are simple and old-fashioned, and have a power that is unforgettable. Masui uses pure Impressionist techniques to depict the sea view (No. 93) and Qingye (No. 92), which is extremely successful. Bnyle is the first of the new-style writers, and the structure and color of his works (No. 15 and No. 16) are modernized and have a unique flavor.

In short, judging from the whole, this Belgian art exhibition can be said to be an exhibition of a certain standard. Ambassador de Giey is enthusiastic about communicating Chinese and Western culture, and Belgian painters are actively participating in the exhibition. In addition to gratitude, we only hope that it can achieve practical success!

Loan Shark Commits Assault, Borrower's Front Teeth Knocked Out 128

Wu Bingjun, a 25-year-old laborer from Henan, residing in Yangjia Zha, borrowed one silver dollar several years ago from Hua Hanqing, a Yangzhou native who specializes in high-interest "rubber ball money" (i.e., exorbitant interest). The agreement stipulated a daily interest payment of six copper coins. Over the past four years, the accumulated interest amounts to over 86,000 copper coins. After partial payments, approximately 12,000 copper coins remain outstanding. Hua has repeatedly pressured Wu to pay off the full principal and interest. Due to lack of funds, Wu pleaded with Hua for an extension, offering to continue paying daily interest. Hua refused, leading to a verbal altercation. Hua then resorted to violence, knocking out Wu Bingjun's front teeth, causing profuse bleeding. Police officers Zhang Shi and Hu arrived at the scene and took them to the Yimiao Police Station for investigation. After interrogation, Chief Liu determined that Hua Hanqing's exploitation of the poor through exorbitant interest constituted a criminal offense. Furthermore, his act of violence due to non-payment was deemed illegal. He was ordered to be handed over to the General Bureau for strict handling.

Ningbo County Security Command Requests Transfer of Suspect in Red Pill Case; Zheng Fengyi and Son Unjustly Arrested, Acquitted in Court Due to Lack of Evidence 129

Zheng Fengyi (also known as Fengxi), a Cantonese native, operates the Yongyuan Pawnshop at No. 285 Park Road and co-owns the Faji Coal Ball Company at No. 10 Meifu Lane, No. 123 Park Road, where he serves as manager. At 9:15 AM the day before yesterday, Wang Yong, leader of the Detective Squad of the Ningbo County Security Command in Zhejiang, obtained an arrest warrant from the First Special District Court and reported to the News Agency Police Station. Together with Chinese Detective Wu Changkai and Western Detective Chief Kainatai, they went to the Faji Company and arrested Zheng Fengyi and his son Zheng Yingyan (23 years old).

Both were arrested on suspicion of trafficking in the narcotic red pills. They were taken to the police station and temporarily detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Division 8 of the First Special District Court. The Zheng family hired attorneys Xue Dubi and Yu Xiangqin to defend them. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's attorney, stated that at around 9:00 AM yesterday, Wang Kuang, leader of the Ningbo County Security Command's Detective Squad, presented an arrest warrant (No. 389) from the court and requested assistance in arresting Zheng Qiuting and Zheng Yangxian, father and son, at No. 9 and No. 10 Meifu Lane, No. 125 Park Road.

This was based on the confession of Chen Yougen, a suspect in Ningbo, who claimed that he was previously a rickshaw puller for Zheng Qiuting and that the Zheng father and son were secretly manufacturing red pills, transporting them to the interior for sale. The police station dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to Meifu Lane. They first entered No. 9 to investigate and found no one named Zheng. Later, at No. 10, they arrested the two applicants in this case. Upon questioning, their names were

Completely different from those on the arrest warrant. Zheng Fengyi stated that Zheng Qiuting was his cousin and was currently in Guangdong, and that there was no one named Zheng Yangxian. The police station conducted a thorough search of the premises and found no equipment for secretly manufacturing red pills or any related documents. Subsequently, Wang, the squad leader, insisted that these were the correct individuals, so they were taken to the police station. When questioned, Zheng Fengyi stated that he operated the Yongyuan Pawnshop and served as the manager of the Faji Coal Ball Company. He had been doing business in this area for over twenty years. He had

Six brothers, three of whom have died. Zheng Qiuting is his third cousin and used to sell coal balls in Hankou before going to Guangdong. His family had no one named Chen Yougen, and there was no rickshaw. Zheng Yingyan stated that he was also known as Kekou and that there was no one named Zheng Yangxian. Wang Yong, the leader of the Detective Squad of the Ningbo County Security Command, stated that Zheng Yangxian had been identified by the confessed suspect Chen Yougen as

Secretly manufacturing red pills for distribution to other areas in their residence in the public concession. Therefore, he came to Shanghai to request assistance in the arrest. Chen also provided clear descriptions of the Zheng father and son's appearance and age, which matched the two individuals apprehended in this case. He requested their transfer. Zhang Tianyin, the police station's attorney, expressed his opinion, stating that the names of the applicants apprehended were completely different from those on the arrest warrant. Moreover, the Ningbo investigators had failed to provide

Sufficient evidence. Even if the two applicants in this case had committed a crime, it would have occurred within the concession. Furthermore, the police station had not found any evidence. He requested that the court order their release to prevent innocent citizens from suffering detention. The attorneys Xue and Yu debated the matter, requesting that the court grant their release to prevent innocent people from suffering imprisonment. They also presented share certificates to prove that Zheng Fengxi was not Zheng Qiuting. Judge Wu Zehan announced in court that the motion for transfer was denied and the defendants were released that day.

Yi Fangshuo Sued Again by Cousin for Loss of Reputation Although Adultery Case Dropped 130

Yi Fangshuo, a comedian actor, has been expanding his business in recent years, organizing the Jingshen Troupe and recruiting young girls to be actresses in the troupe. Yi would then select those who were slightly attractive and easily tempted, using threats and inducements to defile them. As time went on, the matter gradually became public. Last winter, the case came to light, and the French Concession Police Station arrested him and brought him to the Second Special District Local Court, requesting punishment. At that time, Yi's cousin Yi Baozhu, who had been brought to Shanghai from her hometown in Hangzhou by Yi's daughter Yi Meiying and introduced into the troupe as an actress, took the opportunity to report to the French Concession Police Station that she had been living in Yi's house, receiving Yi's training in opera, and had been forcibly raped by Yi. When the police station sent detectives to investigate, Baozhu, at the instigation of Yi's relatives and Yi's wife Hu, withdrew her accusations. Therefore, when the Second Special District Court rendered its judgment, it did not accept the Baozhu's portion of the case. For the remaining part, Yi Fangshuo was sentenced to imprisonment. Until recently, the Second Branch of the High Court declared Yi not guilty, and he was released from prison and moved to No. 10 Minzhi Lane, Nanjing Road, in the British Concession, where he resumed his old profession. However, the prosecutor of the Third Branch of the High Court considered the judgment of the second instance to be inappropriate. He has now submitted a petition to the Supreme Court, raising appeal about the various facts of Yi's crime and the reasons why the second instance judgment was inappropriate, requesting that the judgment be reversed and Yi punished according to law. The Third Branch of the High Court has sent the entire case file to Beijing. Whether Yi is guilty or not remains to be decided by the final judgment. However, his cousin Yi Baozhu's last-minute halt, and not adding insult to injury, was purely because she valued the conditions promised by Yi Fangshuo. Now that Yi has been released from prison, he has no intention of fulfilling his former promises. She hired a lawyer to sue Yi in the First Special District Local Court for compensation for damages, claiming that in 1932, when she was 17 years old, she was introduced into the Jingshen Troupe as an actress by Yi's daughter Yi Meiying. Because she lived in Yi's house, she was raped, causing serious pain to her physical health, mental state, and reputation. She had filed a complaint with the French Concession Police Station in December of last year. Although she withdrew the lawsuit after mediation by relatives and friends, the fact of rape was not eliminated. She was subjected to illegal infringement, so she had no choice but to request the court to order the defendant to pay compensation of 5,500 yuan for her health, mental state, and reputation. As she was unable to pay the litigation fees, she requested permission to be exempted. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang Daxi held a hearing. The defendant Yi Fangshuo did not appear. According to his representative lawyer, Yi had gone to Suzhou. The plaintiff Yi Baozhu was said to be 20 years old, but calculating according to the lunar calendar, her birthday was on the fifth day of the second month, which means she had not met the 20 year adult age. Therefore, she temporarily chose her cousin, Yi Fangchu, Yi Fanghu's half-brother, as her legal guardian. Yi Fangchu stated that his sister Baozhu's chastity had been destroyed by his brother Fangshuo, and she could no longer be married. Moreover, his sister's parents were both dead, and she had no one to rely on. Therefore, he requested that the court order the defendant to pay an amount of 20 yuan per month until she was 60 years old, and he hoped that the amount would be paid in one lump sum. The defendant's lawyer disputed Yi Fangchu's qualifications to represent the lawsuit, as well as whether Yi Fangshuo had committed adultery against the plaintiff. The court then decided to postpone the hearing to investigate the matter further.

Large Wind and Waves at Wusongkou Yesterday Morning, Huangpu River Continued to Experience High Tides, Water Entered Low-Lying Areas 131

Outside Wusongkou, at approximately 5:00 AM yesterday, a sudden and enormous wind and wave occurred. The waves were surging and torrential, creating a very dangerous situation. At that time, ships were entering and leaving the port. To avoid danger, incoming ships dropped anchor and stopped, and outgoing ships delayed their departure. The wind and waves subsided at around 8:00 AM, and the ships resumed normal traffic. When the wind and waves occurred outside the port, the weather in the city was also extremely cold.

Inside the Huangpu River, there were continued high tides yesterday morning, mainly due to the large wind and waves at Wusongkou. When the tide was at its highest, it exceeded the predictions of the Dredging Bureau. Various low-lying roads in the city, such as the area in front of Huiluo Company on Sichuan Road, the area in front of Yong'an Company on Zhejiang Road, and Fuzhou Road, Jiangxi Road, and Guangdong Road, were flooded, with water reaching shin height. The water gradually receded at around 9:00 AM. (Dabai News Agency)
